when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是個程式設計師 , 她確實做了一些事 , 但真正的說法是 , 未來會變得更有意義 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙在1936年之後 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械性的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器是完全理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是來自數學的觀點 , 但告訴我們很重要的 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把數學基礎設置給電腦科學 , 說: 「 不管你怎麼製作電腦的數學基礎 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你是電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 就像babbage , 或電子 , 就像babbage , 或電子 , 就像babbage , 或電子 , 如今 , 電腦的機械 , 如babbage , 或電子 , 如babbage , 或電子 , 如babbage , 或電子 , 就像babbage , 或電子 ,
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它很小 , 所有東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種程度上 , 電腦是有意義的 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做churchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurching
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你接觸到這個連結 , 你說這是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	實際上 , 現今我們所做的一切都能用電腦 , 真的很緩慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	給你一個想法 , 速度有多慢 , 它有大約1k記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會在大約一萬倍慢慢 。
it did have a ram pack .	牠有強烈的包裝 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	你可以加上更多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天我們來到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	這裡有計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在華盛頓 , 科學博物館檔案 , 有數百個計劃和成千上萬頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴布所寫的 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為28的名字 , 也是我先前提到的名字 , 也是一位慈善機構的名稱 , 當時我開啟了這個專案計畫 , 建造出不同的引擎 , 而我們的計畫是要建造出不同的引擎 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯斯頓 , 我們會建造出分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案計畫有幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	第一 , 掃描是babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二 , 目前正在研究所有的計畫 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三個部分是電腦模擬機器 , 最後一部分是用電腦模擬來實現它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成了 , 你就得去看看這件大事 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看到了cpu操作 , 我知道電腦是怎麼運作的 , 但是我看不見這段影片 , 並且說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看到這隻小晶片 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在我們要做模擬的時候 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫 , 他說 , 只要分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來科學的課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 當然 , 他從來沒有建造 , 因為他一直在1940年代 , 改變了 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我會給你們看一段影片 , 說明它看起來像什麼樣子的動作 , 會讓它看起來像動作的影片 , 顯示出一部分是cpu機械工作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以 , 這只是三隻狗 , 還會加上加速器 , 這樣你就可以想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年之前 , 我們會有它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這張圖片中 , 尼安•哈伯特曼在他的作品中展示了人類最近期的作品 , 在這個圖片中 , 《地球上》 , 《家人》 , 《六十億人》 , 以及他的《地球》 , 《地球上》 , 《人類的景象》 , 《人類的景象》 , 在《地球上》的電影中 , 《家人》 , 描繪出了人類對環境的影像 , 透過呼吸拍攝影片來記錄人類的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影師 。

i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我在地球上有很大的影響力 , 以飛行飛行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	在大氣層中 , 大氣層中 , 9噸的二氧化碳 , 這是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談的是生態學 , 我把二氧化碳當作法國人一年 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我必須殺一位法國人 , 當我回到家的時候 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來做我的碳 , 就像每次都一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是展示我們對地球的影響 。

the climate is changing .	氣候變遷 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨絕種 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的演講中 , 理查•尼克斯頓理查•雷尼克博士頓有很便宜、快速基因組序列 , 將健康照護轉移 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療、科學、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體 , 最左邊的 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	底部是性染色體 。

so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你看到的是這四個生物化學信件 , 或我們稱它們為基礎的 , 叫做 「 基礎 」 , 意思是:c、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	在人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億人 ?
is that a big number ?	這是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以推出大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我要在一個基礎上 , 用3 , 000個螢幕 , 我們需要3000個螢幕 , 我們需要3000個螢幕 , 我們需要3 , 000個螢幕來檢查基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 和y染色體一樣 , 會想序列它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年來 , 大約四十億美元後 , 基因組被排序和出版 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後版本發表了 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都在一台機器上完成了 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一塊花費一美元的成本是非常慢的 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	嗯 , 我在這裡告訴各位 , 世界完全改變了 , 沒有人知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在 , 我們做的是基因組 , 我們將這些複製成五十個鹼基 , 然後我們將它們複製成小50的複製 , 然後我們將它們複製成小50的複製品 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	接著 , 我們把這個軟體放進軟體 , 重新組合它 , 並告訴各位故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	為了讓各位看一下這張圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gigabass 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一個在一個星期內 , 一個星期內有兩百個gigabs 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天會改變到600年夏天 , 沒有任何徵兆會變慢 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基礎的價格 , 基礎的價格低了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	等到2011年 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以駕駛木星和火車 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以駕駛到2011年 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以駕駛木星 , 等到2011年 。

so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 人類基因組的能力 , 每年有五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們也知道 , 根據這些機器 , 已經被設置了 。

so a woman is age 37 .	所以 , 女人是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她有兩個雌性乳癌的乳癌 。

six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她回來了血管白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸器衰竭 , 死了八天 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這種婦女被治療的方式 , 大約十年後 , 會看起來像血液 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	由於我同事 , 瑞克•威爾森在華盛頓大學的基因組研究中 , 決定要照顧這個女人的樣子 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他做了序列 , 把所有的基因組組成兩個星期 , 完全沒有大量的基因組 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他把這兩種基因組合成一個特定的基因組 , 另外一個特定的基因叫做tp53 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你有這種特定的基因 , 你90%的可能罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對她的家人沒有幫助 , 但它確實有嚴重、深深的影響 , 若你對她的家人有著深遠的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果它們有相同的突變 , 牠們會得到基因檢測 , 牠們會發現 , 牠們有相同的突變 , 牠們會有同樣的突變 , 牠們會得到基因檢測 , 牠們會發現 , 牠們會有很長的壽命 。

their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們媽媽是個很勇敢的女人 , 不相信這些症狀不在乎 , 透過一些英雄和很多網路搜尋 , 她說服了醫學界 , 實際上他們有其他東西 。

i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 我們有bob , 這是個志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的排列送到整個國家 , 拯救了一名孩童白血病的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	那麼 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個全部的麻醉護士 , 另一位醫生來自我 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob在桌上 , 我們帶著這個小針 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們所做的是基本上 , 透過軟組織組織 , 把這些軟組織放到硬骨頭上 , 每次 , 針對十個骨髓 , 每次都用鼻子 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠帶到護士 , 把牠送到海裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把我帶回來 , 我們再一次地做一次 。
about 200 times usually .	大約有200倍 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	結束時 , 我的手臂很快 , 像瑞士起司一樣 , 像瑞士起司一樣 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序在四十年內沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想起一個最初的新裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 馬row礦工 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	排放的標題 , 其它的運作方式是呈現出來的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的視角病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	不是進入幾十次的前面 , 而是進入前面 , 進入前面 , 再進入骨頭 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性的管子 , 繞著一個特定的線圈圈圈 , 繞著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它可以讓你迅速地啟動 , 很快地穿過一個洞 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們能多次通過同樣的道路 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , 波布只能得到一個刺激、當地麻醉劑 , 並且將它做成一種刺激 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛做了一些原型 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再加上一點點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩個大動物和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 驚訝的是 , 我們發現 , 不只是骨髓 , 我們也得到骨髓 , 我們發現 , 比一般裝置的幹細胞活動 , 比一般裝置還高了十倍 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置是fda在過去一年被用來買的 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活病患者 , 你可以看到它跟著有彈性的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡有兩位在同一個病患 , 同一個病患 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	由於當地麻醉劑量 , 作為一個專家 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們再次重複 , 比起標準方法在同一個病人身上的3到6倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	為什麼你要關心 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成年人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的身體中 , 包括血液的幹細胞 , 在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括我們骨髓裡的幹細胞 , 包括我們血幹細胞的幹細胞 , 包括我們在骨髓裡的幹細胞 , 包括我們血幹細胞的幹細胞 , 包括我們骨髓裡的幹細胞 , 我們已經使用了超過40年的幹細胞 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 針對帕金森和糖尿病產生的骨髓幹細胞治療病人的疾病 , 包括心臟疾病、血管疾病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至神經治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出去 , 今年 , 我們在商業化 , 這一年 , 世代2.0.0.0.0 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望是 , 將更多的幹細胞轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人去簽名 , 來拯救骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可以讓你銀行自己的幹細胞 , 當年輕人更健康 , 在未來應該需要它的時候 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是我們骨髓移植倖存者的照片 , 每年都在史丹福大學 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這科技能讓我們有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和弗雷特•雷特雷特提出了一項爭議宇宙的新模型 , 它是最美麗的新模型 , 可以回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他 , 它是最美麗的新模型 , 它是你所見過最美麗的新模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理 , 科學 , 科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	在他的理論上 , 他理論上所有東西的理論 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	喔 , 去看那些殺人的方程式 。 甜點 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	接下來的18分鐘 , 我會盡力去描述美麗粒子物理學的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 有很多我們可以從珊瑚身上學到的東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚頭上都有數千個獨立的個體 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些池子會不斷突破並分裂成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	假如我們想像這是個超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們就能單獨地問一個問題 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們能問他在這個特定位置的位置 , 跟他的鄰居如果只是機會 , 或命運 , 又或者什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	為了讓溫度升高 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是很有意思的 , 你看到 , 我衝擊了這些珊瑚 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這會持續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居是非常明顯的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在其他的位置也一樣 , 但在其他的位置中 , 卻是不同的人 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分裂成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個超聰明的珊瑚會獨特地準備了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學量子力學非常準確地描述宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實持續分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們來說 , 人類很奇怪 , 因為我們只能經歷一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異 , 是由erwinschrodinger和他的貓所做的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , schrodinger在一個放射性的樣本中 , 由量子力學的原子組成 , 它被放射性 , 由量子力學的原子組成 , 讓它被放射到一個狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本的輻射中 , 釋放毒素和schrdinger已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在其他的現實中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真正的體驗 , 都是每個人的體驗 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	如同所知 , 另一種不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為每個人都只經歷一個獨立存在 , 我們不會看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	像我們一樣 , 像schrodschrodinger在這裡 , 是一種珊瑚會分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學量子力學告訴我們這個世界是如何運作的
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句子中出現:所有事情都可以發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理學的描述是關於描述事情發生什麼事 , 什麼也不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理告訴我們 , 一切都經過幾何和粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	如果這些互動是完美的平衡 , 就會發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來談談我們對這些粒子的了解 , 以及平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 質子和反射光的聚集在一起 , 形成了爆炸的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成一種原子粒子粒子 , 偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這種巨大的機器大型強大的撞擊器在自行車的大型強子撞擊中有17英里長 , 當它運作時 , 將五倍的大型強大的撞擊器在洛杉磯的大型強暴 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法預測特定的粒子會在任何一個撞擊中產生什麼 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量是被質量和能量所組成的 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子比這個能源限制還不夠大 , 我們也不會產生 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼新粒子加速器很令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將能量限制七倍之外 , 這樣我們才能看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到之前我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	這裡有一大堆原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這房間裡的很多人都很擅長推動他們 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	電荷和一個中央的粒子叫做中央粒子 , 沒有電荷和非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 原子中有很大的質量和中子在原子中 , 會產生質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都在左右和右撇子 , 而有反粒子的左派和右手 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉第二代和第三代代代 , 相同的載荷是相同的首次 , 但有較高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子和各種粒子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力電磁力與電磁力互動 , 由粒子稱為光子 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常弱的力量 , 這種弱勢力 , 與左撇子之間的互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強大力力會引起不同的分別:紅色、綠色和藍色
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann , 這些名字是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 重力的作用是重力的作用 , 它的質量和旋轉 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 要了解這裡有不同的指控和所有這些力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量與物質相互作用 , 指導每個粒子的每一個粒子都有 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	未曾見過過的粒子 , 但我們確保存在 , 粒子是希格斯粒子 , 將質量帶到其他粒子 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子撞擊器的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎一定會這麼做 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎就是我們所看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將展示一個美麗的可能性 , 在這個演講結束時 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們把這些不同的粒子用在不同的粒子上 , 用它們不同的粒子和載荷 , 有226 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	有很多粒子會繼續追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	似乎很奇怪 , 自然會有這麼多的基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們把它們排列出來 , 有些美麗的模式就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 電荷是三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個夸克和夸克被組成一個質子時 , 它會產生一個質子 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 相反的粒子 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	實際上 , 電荷是由兩種組合組合:hypercharge和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把這些粒子放在這個二維空間的電荷中 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向上 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力和弱力相互作用 , 製造出這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 未知的電力模型 」 , 它在1967年出版 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部分人都只熟悉電荷 , 而不是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	希格斯在左邊有一個大大的質量並破壞對稱的對稱 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會產生弱勢力 , 讓弱勢力非常弱 , 讓弱勢力非常弱弱 , 讓弱勢力非常弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這張圖片中 , 光子電磁力很大 , 電磁力和電力的光子 , 不管是電磁體 , 都沒有質量的作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁和弱力被描述在二維空間裡的電磁力和弱力 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力的力量轉換成兩條載荷 , 引導引力粒子在這些方向的方向 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有知粒子的電荷都可以被放在四維空間的載荷空間中 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	只要粒子互相交互作用 , 自然會保持在完美平衡的平衡中 , 每一粒相互作用 , 大自然會持續在完美的平衡中 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和一粒子撞撞 , 它會產生能量 , 它在四個電荷中產生一股能量 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都能被創造出來 , 只要它有同樣的能量 , 並維持了零 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這個弱勢力粒子和反粒子可以在撞擊中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 荷荷總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子會撞到電子和中子 , 而這三個仍然加上了零 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的模式不僅僅是如此 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 互動是如何發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	在四維空間中 , 我們能將這個載荷空間轉換為四維空間 , 讓更好的視力互動 , 得到更好的對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強力的粒子中 , 例如綠色 , 用顏色的力粒子 , 例如這個綠色 , 用不同的顏色標示標準 , 例如這個綠色 , 一個強力粒子 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動會在我們體內的每一秒內 , 將原子核聚集在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個主題對三種力量並不結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也能包含兩次重力的引力力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	我們包括這些 , 每一個粒子有兩個不同的旋轉、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分裂了 , 在六度空間中提供一個很好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看到它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	現在 , 這個模式將我們目前所知的知識大自然建立在微小的尺寸中 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是極限的我們能夠達成實驗 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道粒子物理學 , 這些微小的尺寸非常美麗 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的和舊的想法我們不知道 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要擴展這個模式 , 使用數學 , 看看我們能否把這個模式使用數學 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有粒子和力量 , 來創造出我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 來預測新粒子時 , 我們會看到實驗達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理學中有個古老的概念 , 叫做 「 粒子 」 的形狀 , 可以從更完美的模式中 , 和希格斯粒子分開 , 可以從更完美的模式中 , 變成電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新的力量 , 來引導新方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們向新方向提出新方向時 , 我們猜測荷粒子在哪裡引導方向 , 我們猜測荷粒子在哪裡朝方向方向 , 我們猜測荷粒子在這個方向前進方向 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜想 , 我們就能建構標準載荷 , 在六個載荷標準荷荷中 , 由七個荷荷維度所組成的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 這個特定的選擇應對一個偉大的理論 , 由pati和salam在1973年所提出 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的未知模式 , 我們可以看到一些差距 , 粒子似乎被誤解了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是 「 科學研究 」 的理論 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家看起來更大、更大、更多的對稱模式 , 包括建立模式的模式 , 包括建立模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測出存在粒子從未見過的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統計模型預測了存在於兩種新強力粒子的存在 , 它應該和弱勢力相互作用 , 更弱的力量 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七維空間中旋轉 , 並考慮一粒子:第二和第三代 , 對於物質的基本粒子 , 第二和第三代 , 對於物質的基本粒子有相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不獨特地被它們六個載荷所吸引 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準電荷空間的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 若我們在八度空間中找到獨特的新載荷 , 那麼我們可以為每一個粒子產生獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個模式看起來是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二和第三代 , 與第一代的對稱 , 相對稱作 「 試驗 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中 , 實際上是數學中最美麗的幾何結構 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大規模的典型運動團體 , 8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊組是平滑的 , 彎曲的形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個模式的對稱是非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個einsteinsteinsinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinsteinstein
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學 , 形狀的幾何形狀描述所有宇宙如何運作在最小的尺度上 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的形狀存在於八度空間中 , 這種複雜形狀的形狀是非常美麗的 , 它將數千種可能的互動 , 包括這些基本粒子之間的形狀 , 這種複雜形狀的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉時 , 我們就能看見許多其他的細微的圖案被包含在這個 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	透過這個旋轉 , 我們可以看到在八維空間中 , 有一個特定的旋轉 , 可以通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 以八維度的形狀 ,
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 只要我們看到一些洞 , 新粒子被這個模式所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子有20個鴻溝 , 新粒子有20個落差 , 新粒子被稱為patisam粒子 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	在這個圖案中 , 我們知道這些新粒子會像希格斯粒子一樣 , 但有顏色和強力的力量 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填滿這些新粒子 , 給予我們全部的新粒子 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8模式有非常深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是一個偉大的數學美麗可以描述真相與宇宙相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然所描述的數學並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫過: 「 大自然的書 , 已經被寫在數學的本質上 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形、圓圈和其他幾何形狀 , 不論是哪個字 , 都無法理解一個單字 , 而不用在黑暗的迷宮中 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是正確的 , 我也試著跟伽利略論述數學粒子物理學的指導 , 只三角形、圓形、圓形和其他幾何形狀 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我一起工作時 , 數學可以組成一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這數學的心臟是純粹、美麗的幾何形狀 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入了量子力學 , 數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 形成了量子力學 , 數學描述了宇宙 , 形成了量子力學 , 數學描述了我們宇宙的成長 , 和量子力學 , 這數學描述了我們宇宙的成長 , 和量子力學 , 這些數學可以描述宇宙 , 以一個美麗的形式呈現 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的圖形出現在使用新的機器 , 像是大型強子撞擊機 , 我們可能可以看見大型強子碰撞機的大型強子對撞機 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個過程發現的是一個很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到粒子 , 這會非常非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現新粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 很有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是很糟糕的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那麼 , 那會是多麼糟糕 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很糟 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測自然的運作是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的 , 都是長期的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	許多努力工作都知道大部分這些想法可能不會終止對自然 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的理論 , 像是:有很多種子 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論和新型公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有大量的投資 , 就會感到難以放棄一系列的研究 , 不論是怎麼做 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果沒有工作 , 你就得要去嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 唯一能維持保健和不確定性的方法是保持保持和觀點 , 才能保持健康和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我嘗試過最好的我能活平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生命 , 和我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	即便如此 , 即使我所研究的物理學也沒有 , 我仍然知道我已經活過了好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十多年來 , 我住在maui的土地上 , 非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是我最偉大的神秘之一 , 是我的父母 , 如何在所有時間都沒有參與到任何事業中 , 都沒有參與任何事 。

living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	生活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡 , 生活在美麗的地方 , 讓我生活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡 , 生活在我很快樂的地方 。

that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺時所做的 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你從一群的山谷到另一端 , 從一群巢穴到另一邊 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	我想跟我談談這個晚上在昨天發生的 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這令人驚奇的三歲小孩 , 伊斯蘭 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過了人類的歷史 , 家族樹 , 從dna基因遺傳傳遞出來 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是古生物學家 , 拉特•萊克勒 , 他在研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在那之後 , 很不可思議的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在他很常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在非洲尋找人類的早期人類 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以告訴很多關於那些從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中學到的東西 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化化 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他現在認為 , 人類的行為模式很普遍 , 如同我們親近親近親近親近親戚一樣 , 人類的祖先 , 大約七百萬年前 , 人類的祖先 , 和人類的祖先約七百萬年前 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看今天的教科書 , 人類進化的行為 , 你通常會發現人類演化的行為 , 通常會發現人類演化的行為 , 通常會發現人類演化的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他生物還多 , 我們在ted會議中聽到這個ted會議 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 依據我所說的 , 對於黑猩猩的行為來說 , 牠們的行為也很像我們 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個人性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60歲 , 儘管我們認為大部分人可能不會讓它六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	女先生 , 十二歲時 , 她的第一個寶寶在11或12歲 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	此外 , 她有一個寶寶 , 只有五到六年 , 每五或六年都很長一段時間 , 當孩子在照顧孩子時 , 媽媽在晚上睡著 , 並騎著她回來 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 這很長一段時間對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 因為我們是對黑猩猩的學習 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在複雜的進化過程中更重要的角色 , 我們發現 , 學習在不同的形式中扮演著重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察牠們的生長 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們可以模仿行為的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這樣 , 我們相信 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習的行為 , 我們相信 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習的行為 , 我們就能描述這些工具的行為 , 成為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有語言的語言 。 我們剛剛談到的 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們有非常豐富的重複性和姿勢 , 許多相似 , 甚至是相同的姿勢 , 相似的 , 甚至在相同的情況下 , 相似的 , 甚至是相同的 , 相似的 , 甚至在相同的情況下 , 相似的 , 甚至是相同的 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	牠們也吻手 , 握手 , 把手放在後面 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	他們很瘋狂 , 搖搖搖滾 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多許多例子 , 同情心 , 愛和真實的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 牠們就像我們一樣 , 牠們有黑暗的面向 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們是極殘酷的 , 甚至是原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些真正的侵略性行為 , 通常是對鄰居社會團體的行為所造成的影響 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們是非常具侵略性的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物都能幫助我們了解 , 人類和動物王國之間沒有共鳴 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是個非常模糊的路線 , 隨著我們做更多觀察 , 就會變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究 , 一直持續到今日 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 牠們的複雜社交生活在野外 , 使我們意識到我們是沒有分離的 , 和我們共享的地球的複雜社交生活 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到黑猩猩 , 像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 都會失去棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這張照片是從空氣中拍攝的 , 它給你展示森林的高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	當時我在六十年前 , 發現在公園的東方 , 那裡有個問題來到我腦海裡 , 一個問題在我腦海裡浮現了 , 大約16年前 , 當時我在公園的東岸邊緣 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當人們住在國家公園 , 才能拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多的人住在土地 , 可能支持不足 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	數量增加了來自土地的數量 , 和從巴基來的數字增加 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們無法負擔得起買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 tacare 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是個非常有效的改善生活在公園的人們居住村莊 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始 , 現在是24歲 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間去探究 , 但它包含了像樹木護士 , 幾乎沙漠的土地在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、防止土壤消耗 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重新建構土地的農田 , 讓兩年內的恢復效率很高 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力幫助村民從水中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和小群的女性合作 , 提供他們機會 , 給微額貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們在全世界的情況下 , 大約有95%的貸款都被回收 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權婦女教育 , 提供獎學金 , 給女孩們 , 讓他們能夠完成第二次學 , 明白世界各地的女性教育 , 提供獎學金 , 給女孩們 , 讓他們能夠完成第二課 , 明白 , 世界各地的女性教育 , 提供獎學金 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計劃的結果 , 關於保育 , 事情發生了 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育農民在24村居住的農民生活在這個村莊裡 , 而不是看著我們 , 一群白人來研究一大堆猴子 , 而當我們開始研究一系列的農民時 , 其實是坦尚尼亞人在這個村落裡工作 , 而不是看著我們 , 一群白人來研究一群白人 , 研究一大堆猴子 , 和現在坦尚尼亞人一起研究一群白人 , 研究一系列的農民 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	它是坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民們談話 , 問他們對什麼感興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間進步 , 他們開始更了解關於保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 在山丘上高層的山丘是樹木 , 所以你有了很糟糕的土壤和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發我們所謂的 「 更大的黃金球生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這裡是國家公園 , 延伸到各國公園 , 延伸到所有這些非常破碎的土地 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村莊有更好的標準 , 他們真的同意將近10%到20%的土地留在公園裡 , 所以 , 再一次 , 樹木會長回來 , 黑猩猩會有更好的標準 , 牠們可以和其他獨立的土地在國家公園附近的土地進行互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們複製非洲其他地方 , 其它的區域 , 在非洲的其他地方 , 其他的區域 , 受到極端人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲 , 我們一直在討論的 , 主要的問題是 , 幾天以來 , 都是主要的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮很大 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你在土壤上大量居住時 , 絕大多數的人住在陸地上 , 沒有任何地方 , 特別是當你砍伐樹木 , 然後你離開土壤開放 , 讓土壤開放 , 尤其是當你砍伐樹木 , 然後你砍掉樹木 , 讓土壤開放 , 讓土壤開放 , 尤其是當你砍伐樹木 , 然後你砍伐樹木 , 使他們能為自己和家人提供食物 , 為他們自己和家人 , 要怎麼做 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題 , 不只是非洲 , 而是發展中國家的其他地方 , 除了非洲 , 還有其他發展中國家的其他問題 , 除了非洲 , 還有其他發展中國家的其他問題 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	各位知道 , 傑出的科學家 , 艾.威爾森說 , 如果在這個星球上每個人 , 都需要三個新的行星 , 我們就需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說了四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	接下來發生了什麼事呢 ? 我是說 , 在這裡 , 我們是最有智慧的人 , 曾走過地球 , 有著這種非凡的大腦 , 可以用這種技術來解釋 , 來解釋我們所說的 , 最有智慧的 , 是地球上有史以來最聰明的 , 不管是哪裡 , 都能被這些ted會議所發揮 , 但我們卻摧毀了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了一個主要決策之前 , 坐著 , 問自己: 「 這種決定如何影響我們七代前的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策 , 我並不特別談論非洲 , 但開發中國家主要的決策會影響下一個股東會議 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於: 「 這會如何影響下一個股東的權利 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決策影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始旅行非洲各地的問題 , 來到非洲的問題時 , 就會發現越來越多的非洲問題 , 如同我在非洲所遇到的問題 , 會被黑猩猩和它們消失的森林所吸引 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始旅行非洲 , 談到歐洲 , 談話 , 在美國 , 進入亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	各位知道我在談的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣 , 通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在污染我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水水可能是最關鍵的議題 , 我們在這個世紀和全世界都被污染的農業、工業和家庭的化學物質 , 都被污染、工業和家庭的化學物質 , 都被污染 , 被農業和家庭的化學物質 , 都被污染了 , 那些被農業和家庭的化學物質都被污染了 , 似乎是從過去經驗中獲得利益的 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍掉了 , 海嘯的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤問題 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們和其他溫室氣體的溫室氣體排放 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 大家都開始相信 , 我們的氣候問題有很大的錯誤 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混合起來了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人會受到影響更糟 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱變得更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季來臨時 , 它通常會導致洪水、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	居住在一個地區的人口數量 , 居住地點不足 , 無法支援 , 因為整塊土地被降低 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化 , 重覆 , 隨著樹木中的最後一棵樹被砍伐 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只是在非洲 , 而是世界各地 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 讓我驚訝的是 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多年輕人似乎失去希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為可能有某種差異的大腦 , 這種特別聰明的大腦 , ted技術的大腦 , 和同情心 , 說在非科學領域 , 愛和同情心 , 會有什麼差異 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們談話時 , 基本上就是他們對自己說 , 或同情、憤怒 , 和他們說話 , 不論是憂鬱 , 或同情戀 , 或同情 , 我們感覺到自己 , 是因為我們覺得你已經對它有所貢獻 。

the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	樹根和槍擊團體都選三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於他們是哪個國家 , 無論是城市或鄉村 , 哪個國家都在城市或鄉村 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們的設計是從幼稚園到大學 , 有更多成年人開始自己的根源和槍枝 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體選擇 , 三種不同的問題 , 彼此之間互相連結 , 和彼此之間的聯繫 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一項項目就是幫助他們自己的人類社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們有能力 , 他們可能會募資金錢來幫助社區在世界各地 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項項目是要幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 也是動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個項目就是幫助我們所共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	最後 , 所有這些都是學習的訊息 , 在我們的家庭、社區、國家、文化之間、宗教之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間的關係 。

we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們能做出一個很長的清單 , 但很顯然 , 尼爾森•曼德拉在19歲的歷史上 , 被監禁的種族隔離 , 讓他能夠領導他的國家 , 除非血ba的23年 。

and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個說 , 今天我遇見她的年輕女子 , 我遇見她 。

and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 非常令人興奮的是 , 希望明天 , 當她們被賦予權力時 , 有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更好 , 真正是我們希望明天 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家nacohen分享了一些關於塑膠污染的真相 , 關於塑膠污染的真相 , 以及我們生活中有一些關於塑膠污染的真相 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	狄安娜•柯林:粗糙的真相 , 關於塑膠污染 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是一個視覺藝術家 , 我也是其中一個充滿塑膠污染的協調 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋一起工作 , 將我和塑膠袋融合在一起 , 將我和塑膠袋結合在一起 , 將我與塑膠袋結合在一起 , 最後二十年來 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩、三維的雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	大約八年後 , 我的工作開始分裂 , 變成小小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	對於塑膠而言 , 我意識到這是個壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會變得更小一點點 , 因為它總是仍然塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 在海洋環境中 , 有很多東西在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	在過去幾年 , 我了解了太平洋垃圾和gyre 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我的第一個反應是 , 我想這是很多人對學習的第一個反應 , 就是 「 喔 ! 我的天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須去那裡和清潔這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的開發了一個提議 , 要用一艘拖車、一艘船、一艘船 , 一艘船 , 一艘船 , 一台機器 , 和一台超級機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是 , 把塑膠拆開 , 把塑膠放進磚塊裡 , 把塑膠黏起來 , 把塑膠變成垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成垃圾桶 , 變成磚塊 , 可能被用來建造材料在社區裡 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和當地人談話 , 實際上 , 每天都要在海洋環境中和研究塑膠問題 , 我了解 , 實際上 , 要回頭看更大的圖像 , 其實我需要回頭看看更大的圖片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的照片是:我們需要找到一種方法來轉移假裝 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷這些塑膠 , 每天在全球性的塑膠中 , 進入海洋環境中 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 我也了解到我真的很憤怒 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不擔心塑膠 , 可能是你在太平洋的塑膠上所看到的 , 現在我已經知道現在有11個塑膠 , 可能是全世界的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是我所關心的塑膠的塑膠 , 也是塑膠的基礎 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我去超市 , 所有的食物都包裝在塑膠裡 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的平均都包裝在塑膠中 , 甚至是健康食物市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也擔心塑膠的塑膠和毒素從塑膠和毒素從塑膠變成我們的身體
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他的人一起研究這個問題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多倡議我們正在努力 , 但有些非常基本 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果80到90%的海洋中所發現的海洋中所發現的海洋塑膠 , 我們所發現的海洋是塑膠 , 那我們為什麼不稱它為何 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收所有人的書 , 都能持續和綠色的回收 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一個瓶子裡 , 你不需要再想一次 。
what is the reality of that ?	那到底是什麼呢 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 不到7%的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細看 , 尤其是當它塑膠瓶子的時候 , 大部分只會被廢棄或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被循環塑膠瓶蓋瓶 , 再一次塑膠瓶可以再一次塑膠瓶 , 再一次塑膠瓶也不會被塑膠瓶蓋 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件事情是 , 請大家思考一下 , 我們在 「 減少回收 」 三條路上 , 回收: 「 減少 , 回收 」 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	永遠不可能 , 拒絕的塑膠和殘疾的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案 , 有些是很古老的 。

i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想跟大家談談這問題 , 是因為這是個大問題 , 但這是我們所創造的消費者 , 可以解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以解決這個問題 , 讓人們選擇選擇替代方案 。

i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直都在想這個問題 , 是否能否演化或發展出六種感知 , 可以讓我們無可避免地接收到信息 , 或提供我們所能找到的資訊 , 來幫助我們做出正確的決策 。

so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們不太容易取得所有相關資訊 , 可以協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定接下來要做什麼 , 以及行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我的研究團隊在媒體實驗室開發出一系列的發明 , 來讓我們取得這些資訊 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。

phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	伊波菲斯•羅德里格茲和平 , 伊波菲的兒子zacariasrodrizacariasmoussaoui被判定在2001年9月11日的孤立之中 , 愛爾華.羅德里格茲在世貿中心攻擊中 , 發現和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都為了尋找和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都在尋找和平 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題 , 政治 。
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11:她發現原諒、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲利•羅德里奇:我們今天在這裡 , 因為我們有多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但 , 現今 , 感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次知道我的兒子在世界貿易中心在19911年9月11日 。

we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會做些什麼 , 我們的名字叫我們的兒子 , 我的丈夫、家人 , 和家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 很糟糕的 , 震驚了 , 我們的生活中很糟糕的爆發 , 其實 , 我們也沒吃過驚訝 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後 , 當zacariasmoussaoui被指控在六種反對的案例中 , 美國政府被指控為死刑 , 如果被指控 , 我丈夫和我的同伴 , 會對他說話 。

i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲慟中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。

because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我得到立即同情心 。

then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們坐在一個圓圈中 , 支持協助 , 從人體驗到這種解答 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	艾瑞克開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是罪惡或無辜 , 但我想要告訴各位 , 對我的兒子是罪惡或無辜的 , 我不知道我的兒子是罪惡或無辜的 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道它是怎樣的 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該要被公平和懲罰 。 」

and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們所有人都和人類有關 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束後 , 午餐的時間大概是三小時午後 , 我們會覺得我們都知道彼此 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 是一位女人 , 不只能在這些情況下有多大的權力 , 還能為她的兒子做些什麼 , 但她的生活是如此 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這樣的人 , 我從來沒有遇過這種難以置信的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有特殊的連結 , 我非常感興趣 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想 , 這一切都是害怕別人 , 但要做那個步驟 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這不太困難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	誰能見到我不認識的人 , 或我不認識呢 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , 艾瑞莎 , 你有幾個字結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間是上升的 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	艾瑞克:我想說 , 我們得要試著認識其他人 , 另一方面 。

i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了生命品瓶 , 因為我很生氣 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我就像大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節拍下那天 , 在2004年聖誕節拍下 , 當時我在電視上看到了亞洲海嘯的新聞 。

that really stuck with me .	這讓我感到困惑 。

however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於得到了這個 , 生命品質 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 目前為科學界點了 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在航空之前 , 最好的手濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌會穿越200奈米的細菌 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	最小的病毒 , 另一方面是大約25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以 , 這絕對是在200奈米的洞見中 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生活品質是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 什麼都沒有發生 。

instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水 , 用人工程序來做它 , 我們用人造過程來做 , 用人造的過程來做 , 我們用人造過程來做 , 用人造的過程來做 , 我們用母親自然來做 。 她是個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡拿起水源 , 把水從那裡 , 把水從那裡 , 送到山上 , 河流 , 和河流 。

so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 換句話說 , 想想看 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四小時 , 去收集水 。

to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	以此為例 , 英國政府每年花費大約12億英鎊在國外援助 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼停止這樣呢 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	只要有20億美金 , 每個人都能取得安全飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以 , 每年有兩百萬的孩童死亡 , 會活得更好 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪•布魯塞爾說 , 我們生活在歷史上的一刻 , 權力正在改變 , 從未曾過過 , 在華盛頓特區的一場演說中 , 世界各地改變了他所見到的場景 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在十九世紀末 , 詩人寫了一首詩 , 名為英國詩人 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 教科爾的腦袋裡出現了 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是: 「 夏天 , 我聽到一個很遠的距離 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的舞蹈 , 很快地 , 死亡 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩人有興趣的詩人是 「 shropshirelad 」 的詩人 , 詩是 「 shropshirelad 」 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但波爾斯人的觀點是 , 你聽見它 , 尤其是當權力改變時 , 十九世紀的西班牙人會接近我們 , 同時也能從尼爾森的觀點來看 , 溫柔的敘述方式 , 即是長期、熱 , 美麗的石油節目 , 都能接近了 , 同時 , 我們也要進入一個很長期的歷史 , 強烈的氣候變遷 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位先生女士們 , 女士們先生們 , 全都被暴動 , 太常受到血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	而我的信息是 , 若你想 , 身為一個人 , 在這個世界的新勢力開始改變和新勢力的新勢力開始改變和新勢力 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	我們現在看到的 , 通常是很明顯的 , 通常是非常嚴重的時期 , 通常是血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 每世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會說 , 最後一次發生了 , 同事 , 當權力從舊的國家開始 , 歐洲的力量 , 歐洲的大西洋 , 到美國的新興發權 , 過去發生了 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在另一端 , 歐洲權力被用來扮演了兩場大災難 , 最後一世紀 , 在第二個部分中 , 第二個部分是:兩個世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	馬歐文章在歐洲內戰時期 , 可能更準確地描述它們 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中一刻 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我想談談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 兩者是重大的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二 , 我想要提到的新維度 , 這從來沒有發生在現在發生的事 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	咱們來談談關於改變權力的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的情況是 , 很嚇人的是 , 因為從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到一些稍微不同的改變 , 希臘的權力轉變在歐洲文明中發生了 , 但在歐洲文明中 , 我們看到了一些不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅僅是從國家到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也在垂直上移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今 , 國際舞蹈的權力被強迫 , 被監禁的權力 , 被監禁的權力 , 被監禁的權力 , 在國家的權力被監禁 , 被監禁在國際舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談論全球化的全球化 , 但實際上這是全球化的全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	而在國際舞台上 , 國際舞台上 , 國際舞台上 , 國際舞台也不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球階段 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台和全球階段 , 目前為止 , 國際舞台和全球階段的權力 , 實際上 , 國際舞台和全球階段的權力 , 實際上 , 國際舞台和全球階段的權力 , 實際上 , 國際舞台和全球階段的權力 , 實際上 , 國際舞台和全球階段的權力 , 實際上 , 國際舞台和全球階段的權力 , 如今 , 大型金錢的權力 , 將我們所有人的權力轉換為網路的權力 , 國際舞台和全球階段 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球的空間中 , 大部分都沒有規定法律 , 有些人可能會自由限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 這種裝置很強大了 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是為了那些有權力的人在空間空間空間不受限制 , 不規定規定法律被限制了 , 而非規定法律被限制了 , 不僅僅是你想要國際貿易、網際網路等等 , 等等 , 不管你不想國際貿易、網路等等 , 等等 , 不管你不想國際貿易、網路等等等等 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的重點是 , 即使你是世界上最有權力的國家 , 不論你是地球上最有力的國家 , 那些居住的人都可以攻擊你 , 即使你是地球上最有權力的國家 , 即便是地球上最有力的國家 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	意思是說 , 9/11事件中有60%的4000萬美元被送到9/11摧毀的機構 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也使用這個空間 , 網路、衛星廣播 , 可以用來抵禦我們的系統 , 和我們的方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久之後 , 歷史的規則就是權力管理必須遵循 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果我相信這一點 , 那就是我們時間的挑戰之一 , 就是全球化的力量 , 那麼 , 接下來 , 我們的挑戰之一就是將治理轉向全球化 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 數十年來 , 我們已經能夠達成這個目標:要把治理帶到全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	注意到 , 我不是在談論政府 。
