my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順便說一下 , 我自己的觀點 , 女士們先生們 , 各位先生女士們 , 這是不可能完成的 , 透過聯合國的機構來完成 。

but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 要是全球太空的總統 , 我猜猜這不會發生在聯合國機構的創作中 。

the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:治療基礎組織 , 完全依靠基礎組織 , 但 , 強大足夠強大足夠強大足夠強大足夠強大足夠強大足夠強大的美國 , 才能保持最強大的力量 。

now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在 , 有一個問題 , 我們將會再回來 , 假如你把最強大的力量集合在一起 , 來填補管理空間 , 不管是哪些人 , 會因此而死掉 ?

so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 假如你在經歷這些亂流時 , 會變得更不穩定 , 我們的成功 , 會大量地改變我們的能力 , 來讓全球空間變得更不穩定 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看看這開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二個重點是 , 我知道我不需要跟像這樣的人談話 , 但權力不只是轉變平面 , 而是轉變平面 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說 , 歷史文明 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明一直在西方的大西洋中形成 。

we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們從五十年來 , 最不尋常的地方 , 我們在過去的五十年中 , 最不尋常的 , 也是我們所擁有的全球 , 最不尋常的 , 尤其是史上最不尋常的時刻 , 我們所處的環境 , 都必須被它的位置 , 來到華盛頓世界 , 一個全球最不尋常的時代 。

now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	注意到 , 在這個期間 , 你有固定的聯盟國 , 世界各地 , 你有固定的聯盟 , 都被一個蒙諾波世界所控制 。

people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會在世界各地和平共和平 。 」

today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在現代世界 , 由於網路 , 因為這些人在談論的 , 所有東西都與一切有關 。

lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒下 , 全部崩潰 。

we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深、深深地深深地連結在一起 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 國家獨立行動的概念 , 不是與他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為 , 國內國家的權利不足以控制國家本身 , 也因爲美國國家的權力已經開始影響到他們內部的影響 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是一位年輕士兵 , 在英國的小帝國戰爭中 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	敵人就在牆壁之外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁中 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想談談我國家的安全 , 我必須和政府談談 , 是因為我們對安全的威脅 , 我和國內的政府說話 , 因為食物安全是對我的國家造成的威脅 , 我必須跟大眾談談 , 因為食物安全是對我國家的威脅 , 對我來說 , 國際安全的威脅 , 我必須跟大眾談談 , 因為食物安全是對我的國家造成的威脅 , 我必須和大眾談談 , 因為食物安全是對我國家的威脅 , 要談到國內的政府 , 我們的公共事業的基礎建設是對我們的敵人的恐怖攻擊 , 為了我們的敵人 , 我們在公共場所看到的網路戰爭中 , 已經進入了我的國家 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	它不再是美國國家的安全 , 一個國家的安全 , 只是為了讓軍人和軍人的安全 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力可以鎖在一起它的制度 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 實際上 , 我們的政府 , 在工業革命時代的經濟模式上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 基本上 , 建構出了錯的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業知道我們時間的典型結構 , 女士 , 先生 , 這是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	你的能力是網路的重要性 , 包括你的政府和外界 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這裡有第三個法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 如果有第三個法律 , 不要問我之前的第一個法律 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	shown第三法則是 , 在現代時代 , 所有事物都連結在一起 , 最重要的事情是你能做的事和其他人 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的一點是 , 你的結構無論你是政府 , 無論你是企業 , 你的網絡 , 和其他人之間的關係 , 不管你是企業 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在產業中 , 政府也不會這麼做 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是 , 各位先生女士 , 先生們 , 我們現在被鎖在一起 , 以一種方式從未曾發生過同樣的事 , 這也是我們和彼此之間的關係 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體的防禦 , 首次 , 集體防禦 , 是我們國家的概念 , 不再足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前的情況是 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 , 比起他們的盟友 , 我安全 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是這個案例 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互關聯性和武器的規模破壞是 , 我與敵人分享了一場大災難 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我在1970年代 , 與蘇聯聯合國外科醫師合作時 , 在1970年代 , 我們成功了 , 我們成功是因為我們了解我們和蘇聯的關係 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全並不足夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩邊都知道 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人分享了命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東的兩邊 , 都是以色列和平 , 我認為 , 巴勒斯坦人並不了解他們共享集體的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 已經成為我們必須認真思考的議題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩中開始 , 最後我會結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐納的偉大詩歌 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要讓貝殼會死去 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩被稱為 「 沒有人是孤島 。 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	結果是: 「 每個人的死亡都影響我 , 不論是誰 , 貝殼 , 都會影響我 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰•尼 , 是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 我們的一部分是為了我們生存的方程式 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽命和生活方式的道路 , 他分享了9種常見飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們在tedxtt上生長壽命和生活習慣 , 讓他們在tedxtt上播放 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetter:如何活到100+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一個名叫丹尼亞•泰丁的研究發現 , 在某些生物限制中 , 只有10%的人生活在某些生物限制中 , 人類生活在某些生物限制中 , 被我們的基因傳染了 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其它90%是由我們生活方式所決定 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊的:如果我們能找到最佳的生命形式 , 如果我們能找到最佳生活方式 , 我們就能夠找到最佳生活方式 , 以維持壽命的長壽 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人平均壽命的最佳形式 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或是皮膚飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	醫生oz告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重點是 , 有許多混亂 , 使我們活得更好 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你該跑馬拉松或做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃吃有機肉嗎 ? 還是要吃有機肉 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	到供應時 , 應該要帶他們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或復原物質呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的的目的是要怎麼做呢 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神性 ? 我們如何社會化 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們的尋找長壽的方法是與國家地理協調 , 和國家地理協調 , 找到四個人口統計 , 來找出四個人口統計的地理標準 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把一群專家帶到一個專家們 , 去了解這些人做的事 , 將跨越文化的分解 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 這種分裂是怎麼回事 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我要去探討一些常見的迷思 , 到長壽時期 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你試著真的很難活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 只有大約在美國的5000人中 , 只有1500人 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國最快的人口統計數字 , 很難達到百分之一 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們並沒有程式長壽 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被編寫為 「 成功的成功 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家說: 「 年齡是你孩子的年齡 , 你的孩子有孩子時就有孩子 。 」
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	經過演化的效果完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是一隻老鼠 , 或大象 , 或人類 , 就在同一個故事中 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 為了讓它到達100歲 , 你不只需要有很好的生活方式 , 你也必須得到基因學 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以協助緩慢、逆轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 那裡有99個可以讓我們做的事 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球 , 軟骨 , 軟骨 , 軟骨 , 永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會發出 , 我們的腦袋可以發燒 , 我們的腦袋會加上血液 。 我們的腦袋會有血液 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 有35兆個細胞 , 其中有35兆個細胞 , 叫做 「 t 」 , 我們在說國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	每八年 , 這種細胞會自動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們轉動自己 , 就會損傷 , 損傷就會損壞 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它的建構指數增加了 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有些時候 , 我們都拍了一首歌唱片 , 讓朋友複製那首曲子的錄音帶 , 然後讓我們的朋友複製這首歌劇的複製品 , 讓朋友複製那首曲子 , 很快地 , 讓我們的朋友複製了那首曲子的錄音帶 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人比一個125歲的老人更快了125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有什麼能讓你衰老、停止老化 , 我在做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最重要的是最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體、身體、身體 , 90年來 , 比較多的女性 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的預期壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	在這條路線上 , 我們留下了12個好處 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們都能得到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 大部分的慢性疾病、心臟疾病、癌症和糖尿病 , 都沒有 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 最好的方法就是去看這些世界各地的文化 , 讓這些年齡的人口數十年來 , 比我們更大 , 中年人口的壽命 , 中年死亡率的數量是 , 中年死亡率的百分之十倍 , 尤其是在這個國家中年齡的人口 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍色區域大約125英里 , 在義大利的海岸 , 在義大利的海岸 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 島嶼有一百四十萬人 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有這個區域 , 居住最長的人 , 比我們在美國這裡有百分之十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡是人們不只到達100歲的地方 , 他們做得很棒 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡102歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去工作、砍伐木頭 , 還能比他們更年輕 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實回到基督徒的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是被隔離的古老文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是牧羊 , 大部份是牧羊 , 主要是牧羊 , 牠們大大是牧羊 , 牠們主要是牧羊 , 大量是牧羊 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是植物為基礎的飲食 , 可以帶到田野 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	牠們拿出一塊麵包 , 叫做卡塔卡塔音樂 , 由灰色動物組成的 , 而一種葡萄酒 , 比任何已知葡萄酒的葡萄糖更高 , 而葡萄酒 , 含有3脂肪酸 , 而一種葡萄酒 , 含有三倍的葡萄糖 , 而一種葡萄酒 , 比任何已知葡萄酒的三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密我認為謊言是他們組織他們的社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最好的一部分是如何治療老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎高峰在24歲時 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 年紀越多 , 你就得到更多的智慧 , 擁有更平等的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你在沙丁尼亞看到一個月曆 , 而不是看到月曆的百分之八十 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 對於這些家庭的父母來說 , 對於父母來說 , 他們的壽命率較低 , 比起死亡率 , 更低的死亡率和低估率 , 死亡率和低降低率 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現在地球另一邊的另一邊 , 大約800英哩的南方 , 阿基奇島的阿基奇島 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主要島嶼的北部 , 這裡是全球長壽的三角洲 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這裡是最古老的居住女性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這是一個地方 , 人們在世界上最長的壽命不可預期 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們生活很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 牠們在睡眠中很快 , 很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比平均壽命更長了七歲 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍之多的美國人 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	第五分之一是乳癌和乳癌 , 在美國的大殺人 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化已經給予這些數字建議 , 讓他們能教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物的飲食 , 很多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約八倍 , 像美國人一樣 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	更重要的是牠們吃的食物 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種各式各樣的策略 , 不管你知道的 , 這是美國最大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們吃掉較小的盤子 , 所以他們會吃少數的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	而不是服務家人 , 把食物放到桌上 , 然後把食物帶到桌上 , 把食物放到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的年齡 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由於混亂所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食習慣 , 例如哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、漢堡 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單的說法是 , 有人說 , 在他們的胃口中 , 要提醒他們要吃掉他們的胃 , 只剩下百分之八十 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	花了半小時才能從你的大腦中傳送到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	只要記住停止80%的幫助 , 就能協助你做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞一樣 , okinawa有一些社會結構 , 讓我們能和長壽 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立殺死了 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五年前 , 平均美國有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 在你人生中出生時 , 你出生於一個系統中 , 你出生於一個系統中 , 你出生在五十多個朋友中 , 你出生在你自己的人生中 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為moai 。 如果你在moai , 如果你在一個月球上 , 如果你在一個月球上 , 你總是有一些人有你的背後 , 會有你的遺傳 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特殊的媽媽 , 這些五位女士已經聚集了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把我們的成年分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們有工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 它的意思是要退休到亞利桑那州去高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在科納瓦語中 , 甚至沒有一個字可以退休 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	反而有一種詞是 「 基加西 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗糙地翻譯 , 意思是: 「 你早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這個102歲的大師 , 他的kigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigai在
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這百歲的漁民而言 , 牠一直在捕魚魚 , 一週就要捕魚 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 美國國家研究院 , 實際上給了我們一個問卷 , 給予這些百分之百的人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 人們常常感到困惑 , 不論是誰 , 他們都很困惑 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們很明明為什麼在早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這個102歲的女人 , 她的愛吉加爾只是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾經歷過
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩分離了101年半 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 覺得自己會覺得什麼樣子 , 感覺就像是被一位曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭放回來 , 她說: 「 感覺像是跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我編輯的編輯想要我去找美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	儘管我們看了明尼蘇達州的詩人 , 那裡有非常高的百分比 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們找到美國最長壽的族群之一 , 住在洛馬琳達 , 加州 , 加州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	抗議者是保守法者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們在星期六 , 星期五日落在星期六 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	《24小時的監獄》 , 他們稱之為:
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 來傳達他們非凡的長壽 , 相對的 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的預期壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但 , 對於一位女性 , 他們的壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異更大 , 比起美國人的預期壽命長達十一年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究顯示了約七萬人 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	嚴謹的研究 , 我覺得它很明顯地說明了這個藍色區塊計畫的承諾 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個不可思議的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	白人、黑人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共享的就是一組非常小的生活型習慣 , 習慣他們常常生活中最常見的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中取得他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:章魚:章魚 , 百分之三十二的綠色植物 , 通常是肉類 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在時間非常嚴肅的時候就這樣做 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論有多忙碌 , 他們會停止一切 , 專注於他們的社會網路 , 然後在宗教上 , 大自然行走 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量是 , 每週一生都在做偶爾 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	這一切都很困難 , 不需要錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	阿德維主義者也傾向於其他的抗爭者 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一場參加會議的派對 , 你看不見人們穿著jimbeam或rollingjimbeam 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們說的是他們的下一天性步行 , 改善 , 是的 , 祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們對彼此的影響彼此深遠且可測量 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 讓ellswhareham 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellswhareham97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個多百萬富翁 , 但當收入者想要六千美金來建立隱私權利時 , 他說: 「 我會這樣做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 在接下來的三天 , 他穿著水泥 , 包圍著周圍的環境 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預測的是 , 也許 , 在第四天他結束了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在桌上的人 , 做開頭手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97歲時 , 每個月他仍然有20個開放手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	老鼠 , 十三歲 , 一隻活躍的牛仔 , 早上游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末 , 他喜歡放進板子上 , 丟下樓梯 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從那一天開始 , 用重量來實現 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在聖貝納丁諾爾斯維爾的路上留下了七個不同的組織 , 在那裡她仍然自願為七個不同的組織提供七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在19個硬幣的探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一你會見過的人 , 他在撒哈拉沙漠沒有陽光 , 他的腳踏車穿過沙漠 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我會告訴你們 , 沒有冒險的比起飛行車騎腳踏車的高峰 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 。 」 她告訴我 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這些三種文化中的共同點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	什麼是他們所做的事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	然後我們管理了九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們做了兩種藍色區域 , 由這個和這些共同的點子組成 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我是要把這句話放在這裡 , 沒有任何練習 , 至少我們思考練習的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了他們的生命 , 讓它們不斷地被重視為實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些一百歲的兒童都在地上坐下 , 她們坐在地板上 , 每天有30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子 , 樓梯上樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每趟旅行、教堂或教堂 , 或教堂 , 或朋友的房子 , 每次旅行 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 去做房子工作或做房子 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	這種燃燒的卡路里就像跑跑跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做實體活動時 , 他們都傾向於有花園 。 他們傾向於有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何在正確的狀態下做出正確的權利 , 所以他們有正確的權利 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每種文化都有時間轉變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 七天的聖戰者祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawan有這個祖先的祖先 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在心血管疾病時 , 會觸發一種稱為 「 氣味反應 」 的症狀 , 引發了 「 氣味反應 」 , 它和所有阿茲海默症患者有關的心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你慢下來十五分鐘時 , 會產生一種更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有用詞彙的意義 , 例如 , 阿肯尼亞瓦 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的一年 , 是因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及年復一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的人生 , 值得約七年的時間 , 值得約七年的時間 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	反而 , 這些人每天都喝了一點點 , 不是賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們通常會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 但很多豆類和甜蜜 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略要從桌子上擺脫 , 讓它們從桌子上 , 隨時隨地 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接下來的基礎是他們如何聯繫 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先把家人帶進來 , 照顧他們的孩子和老年人 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於一個信仰的社群 , 值得花4年的時間 , 預期壽命只有四倍 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 他們也屬於對部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	不論是生成或他們正常被自己和對人的身分交配 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從fm研究中發現 , 如果你三個最好的朋友越過胖 , 你就會有更好的機會 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人聚在一起 , 那將會有很大的影響力 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你的朋友喝了一個小東西 , 沒有太多 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝酒 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但不太多 , 他們的確是實體活動 , 會有大規模的衝擊 , 和信任 , 和信任 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不在歷史上 , 全世界的人口數量超過百分之二 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常在一月開始 , 通常是十月份 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	長壽以來 , 沒有短期治療 , 不用藥丸或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但 , 想想看 , 你的朋友是長期冒險的旅程 , 所以 , 或許你能做的最重要的事情是 , 花了數年的時間 , 去你的生活 , 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	基礎上 , 卡塔馬塔rinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarina:
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarina:
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有個朋友在葡萄牙 , 他的祖父 , 騎腳踏車和洗衣機 , 他可以交通他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他不知道如何建造一台車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有一段時間我們了解他們如何運作 , 以及它們如何運作 , 我們了解它們如何運作 , 以及它們如何運作 , 所以我們可以建造並修復它們 , 至少能做出改善的決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在二十世紀 , 許多這些人在二十世紀時就失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造家社區和開放式的模型正在帶領這些知識 , 關於它們如何運作 , 以及它們在我們生活中所產生的結果 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 創造出各種知識 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統的材料 , 像是紙、紡織品 , 以及它們如何製造出來 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚訝、有奇異的塑膠 , 改變顏色的塑膠 , 改變顏色的塑膠 , 會改變顏色 , 製造出電力 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我舉個例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	電路板的電路板或電路板也不會使用傳統列印電路板或電路板 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個小小的例子中 , 我們用它來製造一種觸覺感應器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來創造觸感感應器 ,
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	過去的藝術家最近發展指出 , 我們很快就能夠用在雷射印表機和筆筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張圖片是由無色的光明散射粒子組成的 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是 , 雖然一般的光線繞過整個表面的光線 , 我會把光線轉換在邊緣 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這項材料包含了內部設計和多個觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	氣候變色的顏色會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在溫度上 , 放在一個溫度上 , 比你能看到的狀況更高 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒瓶子中 , 要讓內容很酷 , 可以喝酒 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	所以這些只是一些常常被稱為智慧材料的東西 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會在我們每天使用的物品和技術上使用 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行汽車科幻小說 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 改變顏色的溫度、鍵盤、鍵盤 , 並且窗戶會轉變為光線 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我為什麼今天要談的是智慧材料呢 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造者 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇他們是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何運作的 , 但我相信我們應該更深入了解我們所創造的組合 , 而現在 , 我們並不知道這些高科技的組合成我們的世界 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以使用它們 , 很少有人說他們是如何製造的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們大部分在交易秘密和專利只有大學和企業都可以取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 凱西.男生和我開始了一個專案 , 叫做 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是個網站 , 我們每一個人都想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 ,
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們會把它變成大大集體的資料庫 , 用智慧型材料來製造資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們要關心智慧材料是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何運作的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的事物 , 以及我們無法形塑我們不了解的東西 , 以及我們無法形塑我們不了解的東西 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們所穿的衣服 , 我們所穿的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 我們所穿的衣服 , 我們所穿的衣服 , 我們所生活
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個充滿智慧型材料的世界 , 我們應該知道 , 了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 重要的是 , 創新總是被吸引者 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 演員、個人電腦、飛機都不是專家 , 而是從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學的兩位科學家 , 他們發表了一篇論文 , 用簡單的方法來製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬丹•布希克曾經歷過化學 , 直到讀了這篇論文和工具 , 完成了實驗的實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了一個烤箱 , 甚至製造了自己的創作 , 他甚至製造了自己的蒸汽水 , 甚至製造了自己的蒸汽水 , 甚至製造了自己的蒸汽水 , 甚至製造了自己的蒸汽水 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過的結果 , 而沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並繁殖 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬丹的主要創新就是在一個實驗中創造出一個實驗 , 在芝加哥的實驗室建立了一個實驗 , 在芝加哥使用唯一便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己做 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這份工作 , 其他人可以挑選他出版的作品 , 其他人可以選擇他出版的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想要提倡她的專案是要提高專注在創造力和技能上創造力和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 教導我們學習如何運作 , 但在他們的設計中 , 教導我們如何運作 , 他們教導我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	漢娜的另一方面 , 則是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常物品的技巧 , 用來創造出不尋常的物品 , 用來創造出不尋常的物品 , 用來創造出不尋常的物品 , 用來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來協助我們製造出不尋常的物品 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	漢娜 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一些銅板 , 上面是一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一些銅板 , 上面有一些銅板 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	因此 , 由於麻省理工學院的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的文件 , 用簡單的銅板指出的材料 , 來製造一系列的紙 , 用簡單的銅板來製造 , 來製造一系列的紙 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和其他作家一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的文章 , 讓任何人都能複製並繁殖他們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學中最承諾的之一之一 , 它允許我們創造便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的作品 , 實際上她分享她的發現 , 開放了一系列新的可能性 , 包括美感和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	有趣的是 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 我們不會害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常處理問題從不規定的角度來看 , 在過程中 , 最終發現了替代方案 , 甚至更好的方法來做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造出自己的知識 , 越多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出他們的知識 , 更好的機會 , 就能創造出科技 , 才能真正保存我們 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我感覺有點像tednelson在1970年代初期所做的 , 他寫道: 「 你必須理解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主人 , 只有科學家關心 , 而沒有人夢想在家裡 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你必須了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 先知新興科技是最好的方法 , 來確保我們在未來的對話是有意義的 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會用預測模型來計算安全的安全路線 , 讓每個人在道路上 , 用預測模式來計算安全的路線 , 讓每個人在道路上 。 但如果車子可以跟我們分享資料 , 並且用預測模式來計算安全的路上每個人的安全軌道 , 不意外地 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛.赫爾:如果車子可以說話 , 意外可能會避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	咱們來面對:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	我們不想這樣做 , 但事實上 , 宗教信仰和幸運的地板在世界各地的地板上被我們所認知的事實證明了 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國造成死亡率的75% , 造成死亡率和百分之七十五的死亡率 , 沒有任何藥物或酒精 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以說清楚 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時在高速公路上 , 車子在我面前 , 我看到布拉克燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢慢下來 , 我會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上腳踏車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不會慢慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停止 , 死亡停止 , 死停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	僅僅是65到零 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我打掃了 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 車子完全沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道車子停止了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 讓車子互相交流 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是希望你們稍微想想一下 , 駕駛的經驗是什麼樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 , 關上門 , 你在玻璃泡泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受到你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的工作任務 , 在超human的速度上 , 超human的速度 , 超human的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你必須指導你是兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	沒錯 , 所有人都沒有設計這個任務 , 但人們要求你做些事情 , 例如:你要做些什麼 , 第一件你要做的事 。
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛放在道路上 。 那是對的 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看著你的盲點 , 向下走路 , 不要看你在哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你們和其他人 , 這是安全的方法 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要做呢 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我看看這裡嗎 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一件很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上做些什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們錯過了一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會覺得錯了 , 或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數個意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒有看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在 , 科技可以協助我們改善 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 我們將能夠看見這些車子 , 不只在三輛車上 , 和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥類的眼睛 , 我們就能看見這些車子的外面 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能看到在我們面前的車輛 , 看到車輛的速度是多快 , 或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個傢伙在零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 不用車子 , 不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維空間的物體 , 有著固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在路邊走路 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在公開的路上行駛 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於車子的未來來說 , 很難做出合理的預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車上 , 摩托車和摩托車 , 摩托車和摩托車 , 摩托車和摩托車 , 一小時後 , 我知道你有了這個經驗 , 沒有 「 只是從無人 」 來了 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人已經在路上半小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英哩 , 有人看過這個傢伙 , 他在地圖上 , 地圖上 , 很快地圖上 , 他就在地圖上 , 地圖上 , 他在地圖上 , 很快地 , 他就在地圖上 , 直到地圖上 , 他在地圖上 , 很快地 , 他就在地圖上 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為那輛車會知道 , 因為那輛車會知道 , 因為那輛車會在他的耳朵中說: 「 五分鐘、摩托車、摩托車、摩托車 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出合理的預測關於汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	那麼 , 我們該怎麼辦到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從一些簡單的資料開始 , 只要分享我們在車輛的位置 , 分享的資料 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我在車上有一台攝影機 , 我有一個很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有很精準的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	用電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子 , 和他們在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他汽車一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有精確的點子 , 和其他車輛的概念 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車子分享資料 , 如果他們互相對話 , 會怎麼辦 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	教授和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬結果 , 當汽車共享gps時 , 我們已經把這個研究應用在電腦模擬上 , 例如:鋼索攝影機、gps , 和電腦模擬測驗的同時 , 我們已經把這個研究應用在電腦模擬中 , 當汽車共享gps時 , 我們已經把這個研究應用在電腦模擬上 , 讓電腦模擬結果在兩位前面的感應器 , 正常用電腦模擬器 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也用了微妙的溝通線索 , 機器人彼此互相溝通 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相交流時 , 它們會追蹤彼此的位置 , 以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在把更多的機器人加入混合物中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你太太聊天的時候 , 很難處理所有的包包 , 所以你必須優先考慮 , 所以你必須優先考慮 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人卡車正在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你就不會注意到這些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你最先把一個人看得很小 。
that guy could be a problem .	這傢伙可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會死去 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道駕駛你需要什麼駕駛才能避免 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要做的是如何讓每個人都能做到最好 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼會說: 「 你得不得不得出路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它依賴兩件事:一個 , 汽車的能力 , 以及第二位駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在電話或你知道 , 做一些事情 , 他們不可能會在最好的位置上對緊急狀況做出反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一系列的研究做司機狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列三台攝影機 , 我們能偵測到 , 駕駛者正在往前看 , 看著手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測 , 誰 , 車子 , 最好的位置可以預測誰 , 車子在最好的位置 , 可以預測出誰 , 車子是最好的位置 , 可以預測誰 , 車子在最好的位置 , 可以預測出誰 , 車子在最好的位置 ,
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術現在存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們所面對的最大問題 , 就是我們自己的願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是一個很不舒服的概念 , 這點子 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 和其他車子一起走路 , 說我們會在海邊走路 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以被用來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我看著你的車子時 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	假如我看你的清單板數字 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後背後面向 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位想像一下 , 如果你真的不希望你被困擾的青少年 , 你會死去 , 停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過分享我們的資料 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 咱們來看看你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xpringenhawkerpeterdiamandis談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金斯說他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金 , 讓太空飛上大氣層面 , 並且從中空中 , 以無形的速度 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	企業、飛行、科學、短說、空間、科技、宇宙 。

and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 地球上唯一一種方式是自行飛行、無重的飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿飛機 , 飛到頂端 , 你就無25秒了 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回到下面 , 你重重兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	再一次 , 再一次 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你能得到8 , 10分鐘 , 太空總署的太空人如何訓練他們太空人 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。

medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫師davidbolinsky現在有三分鐘的刺激 , 顯示在細胞裡的生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•鮑林斯基y動畫了細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我從不同的觀點來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 我一直在看 , 從我長大後 , 真相和美麗在科學的表達、真相和美麗的表達 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是美麗的理想 , 由科學和數學 , 結合起來 , 真相和美麗的理想 , 是因為科學和數學的理想 , 其實是很美好的 , 由於科學和數學幾乎像理想的結合 , 會被科學和數學結合 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達是真實的表情 , 說是真實的表達 , 意思是 , 你能做些什麼 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	他們是很有力的 , 不可行的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨特的 , 有時常常很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以從螢幕上看 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美麗是常常在科學領域中被忽略的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是以一種方式來描述美麗的事物 , 尤其是當你了解語言和美麗的語言 , 和美麗的人們會被表達出來 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學的平方 , 假設你看到生命必須從數字描述宇宙的角度來解釋 , 宇宙中有著一個錯誤的理想 , 直到你看到生命必須從數字來描述宇宙 , 這些都是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我當作醫學博士時 , 我就被教導 , 透過使用動畫來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用影像 , 透過使用動畫 , 透過使用動畫 , 透過使用動畫 , 透過使用圖像 , 透過使用圖像 , 透過使用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過利用動畫來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過利用動畫來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用動畫來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生們常常在一個環境中學習 , 他們所學到的是真相和美麗並不總是有證據 , 但他們被教導的事物是很有真相和美的 , 而不是總是有證據 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是一塊雞肉的古老食譜 , 把雞黏到味道上 , 還沒錯 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣做對我們的學生 。

so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始研究一個專案 , 研究細胞生物學的真相 , 讓學生可以理解更大的圖片 , 讓他們能夠理解更大的圖像 , 來探索這些事實 。

and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微生物的心臟是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微型機制 , 是由胺基酸所組成的基礎、精準、精準、精準、精準、精準、精準、精準、精確的裝置 。

and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 把這些視覺應用在腦袋裡 , 讓這些學生能夠找到真正的生命 , 像是哈佛大學的生物學學生 , 像是哈佛大學的博士學位 , 這些學生會被激發的觀點 , 將它們的視覺呈現出來 , 讓它們能夠真正地了解 , 生命如何讓這一切發生 , 真正的 , 生命是如何運作的 。

we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們做了一個主題 , 例如 , 牠們在骨骼的外面 , 看到和感知 , 牠們在附近的水面上 , 觀察到外面的細胞 , 裡面有噴霧器 , 牠們會從細胞中吸收到外面的細胞 , 而它們會從細胞中吸收到外面的資訊 , 牠們會被吸收到外面的細胞 , 牠們無法看見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到了這些資訊 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 來改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 來改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們改變它們的形狀 。

and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	我要展示給你們看的 , 是我們製作的第一面鏡頭 , 它是一支三分鐘的閱讀器 , 它正在進行一個計畫 , 接下來要花四到五年的時間 。

but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內部的運作 , 其實是非常驚人的 , 它們其實是生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器都能與彼此互動 。

and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出這些部分 , 從資訊中從原子核的分子 , 到基因 , 到基因 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有這些小小的生命 , 沒有這些小小的生命 , 沒有這些小小的生命 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在這些機器中 , 克里斯 , 實際上 , 真的很不可思議 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是fedex的dart細胞 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他採取了一堆新的製造蛋白質 , 包含所有品牌新製造的蛋白質 , 不管它是否需要細胞 , 不管是用細胞膜 , 或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西正在運作 , 現在 , 在你一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以不論你感覺到什麼 , 你都沒有什麼 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當我回家想想看 , 我們的大腦有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想一些我們正在學習細胞機械的方法 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們意識到 , 我們就知道 , 到底發生了什麼事 , 我們將會有多久 , 我們就能夠控制我們的健康和未來的世代 , 以及我們要怎麼做 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個發現更多的真相 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但真的很令人驚訝 , 這些細胞 , 這些細胞 , 需要這些微型的細胞 , 需要他們做些什麼 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 , 讓細胞做得做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起合作 , 協助我們的身體巨大 , 讓他們無法見見功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃在她的旅館去年 , 看到國家 , 但當憂鬱症和她的婚姻在她的旅程結束時 , 她的經歷變成了無家可歸的 , 一個美好的家庭 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪.布朗頓:我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我知道如何做很多新的事 , 二十二年來當記者 , 我學到很多新事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到要做的事是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了無家可歸的一家 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉我父親在二月份工作的報紙編輯 , 決定要旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死子非常辛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事時 , 我想要感受到很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一直都在旅行 。 我決定住在一個旅行的旅行中 , 一年會像一趟旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包了我的貓 , 我的車子 , 開車到日子 , 完全失敗了三件重要的事情 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會平均生活在永久的結構中 , 甚至是一個人 , 一個人的社會平等 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我失敗了 , 了解到別人對別人的負面感知如何影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓他人實現 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我失明無家可歸是態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	第一 , 生活在火車上 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在校園裡 , 常常打開 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 憤怒和憂鬱 , 是我父親的死亡 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須得到一份全職的工作 , 才能支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	最近的熱夏天夏天是非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	到公園裡 , 沒有很明顯的貓和狗狗和我一樣 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓在火車上飛過了一輛開窗的窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗在那天花了點心 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我在辦公室大樓和卡車停車時 , 我會用員工來表演 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者我在公共場所的房間裡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚時期的溫度高達80度以下降到華氏80度 , 讓它很難或不可能睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物是熱中的食物 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰冷的冰塊在三十幾小時內就變得很糟糕
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法負擔得起一間公寓 , 不能負擔得起公寓 , 不能負擔得起公寓 , 不能負擔得起公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕把它們放出來 , 所以我留在火車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱讓我太生病時 , 我用了一塊桶子 , 用一桶垃圾桶 , 用一桶垃圾桶 , 用一桶垃圾桶 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣溫下降時 , 溫度下降了 , 溫度下降了 , 溫度下降了 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一個全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停下來 , 我會避免注意到 , 被警察攔截 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺到我人生的掌控 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道 , 或它發生了什麼事 , 但後來我從一位有名的名作家和記者 , 變成了無家可歸的家人 , 和記者 , 身為無家可歸者 , 身為無家可歸者 , 身為一個無家可歸者 , 讓我呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商 , 沒有變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天賦、我的價值觀、我的價值觀 , 所有我都不一樣的東西 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我送到一個無家的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 三天內就沒有洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和憂鬱症一樣 , 和憂鬱症的人一樣 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾位無家可歸的人發現 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 , 你為什麼會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人 , 卻沒看到我 , 卻沒看見我 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 。 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	藥品藥物給我的反應 , 讓我憂鬱症患了我自殺 , 我心想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 我還記得心想: 「 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 很久以前 , 她聽說 , 布魯斯特 , 一個全國性的記者 , 一直在談論我 , 全國的新聞報導 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇文章 , 是在提姆的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	當時他正在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrussert在walmartstimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussert
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它到達那裡的地方 , 我是作家 , 還是我是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書 , 我找到了tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 然後我把我的文字寫下來 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久後 , 我搬到田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我生活在一個旅館裡 , 與朋友交流 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	接下來的夏天 , 我是記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎勵 , 我住在我自己的公寓 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再看不見了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人工作 , 生活在車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續犯罪化 , 或在車子上或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸、無家可歸 , 主要仍然隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你見過一群人 , 他們鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵她們 , 鼓勵她們 , 鼓勵她們 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類精神可以克服任何事情 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不在這裡是無家可歸的女兒 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是在這裡鼓勵你去鼓勵你去給你所見的下一個巴哈德勒 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位的是 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們生活在哪裡 , 或他們生活在哪裡 , 或他們生活在哪裡 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我在walmart停車場停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , tedxchange , thailand " mr. " dom , 美國的 「 domr 」 , 來源自於1970年代 , 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克 , 非常有效的談談保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	伊維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉維拉
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	二十年前 , 我在貧窮時 , 許多人生活在貧窮 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們沒有從福利計畫或貧窮的計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃開始 , 追蹤一個非常成功的兒童健康活動 , 活動的活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:讓孩子們接觸到母親 , 然後跟隨家庭計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是孩子的死亡率 , 你也需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回到我們為什麼要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	7個孩子在3.3%到3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們很少醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有得到答案 , 我們不把問題當作一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士和婦女 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 來解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	這很美妙 , 但它只佔了20%的國家 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	另外百分之八十的人會說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以 , 我們去了普通人你看到的 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 在那黃色的標誌裡 , 我希望他們還沒拿過 , 因為有 「 cocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacocacoca
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那時我們比可口可樂還多 。

they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	在社區中 , 他們知道客戶通常是對的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很熟悉 , 客戶總是對的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很清楚 。

so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們去找那些被視為是解決方案的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論你在哪裡 , 都能看到船隻 , 販賣香蕉、螃蟹 , 還有避孕法 , 你會在泰國買到的 , 賣出香蕉和螃蟹 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天教教堂非常強壯 , 而泰國人是佛教徒 。

so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去了教師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過四分之一的收穫是關於家庭規劃 , 一個新的字母、a、b , 為生育 , 為了保險套 , 用新型的字母 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	接著 , 我們有蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你會丟掉 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	若你在任何事前都行得通 , 你就向前邁進 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如 , 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥丸 。

uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了保險套 , 很棒 , 叔叔 , 叔叔 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 , 再來一次 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	再一次 , 教育 , 班娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做這件事 。

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們正在努力解決的問題 , 同時我和其他20位在romott工作的專家 , 正在努力解決這個問題 。

and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是一個非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型、可攜帶的機器人 , 不僅僅是負擔得起的 , 而且它必須成為人們真正想要帶回家和孩子的孩子 。

and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過使用iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 可以在過去 , 使用iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造一個機器人 , 裡面有超過150美元 , 這種機器人在過去有150美元 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當羅馬登入時 , 他就在創造模式 。
