he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	牠從鳥類的訊息傳遞出來 , 這是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板時 , 我們看到他正在努力的地圖 , 紅線延伸到所有洞穴的地圖 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 我們就完成了這個循環 , 你知道的 , 你必須做的就是閱讀這些文章 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院學院學院的研究者 , 不是建造東西 , 我們能創造出材料 , 建立自己組合的結構 , 來建造一些東西 , 我們能創造出自己組裝的材料 , 可以製造出自我組裝的樣子 , 像是在自我組裝的過程中 , 可以製造出自己組裝的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	太陽能板 , 可以讓我們自己做些東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我要向你們展示我們製造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 我們的建築物和機器會自我組合 , 複製並修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要向你們展示我所相信的目前的製造過程 , 然後將它與某些自然系統相比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在現有的技術上 , 我們有天花板 , 兩年半的時間 , 大約有五十萬到一百萬個部分 , 非常複雜、新的、令人興奮的科技 , 包括鋼、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有很興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五百萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 有兩百萬種類型 , 或dna , 或dna中有兩百萬種類型 , 可以摺疊在大約一小時之內 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統中有很多複雜的系統 , 但它們非常有效率 , 比任何我們能建造的東西更有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建造的東西更有效率 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們很難犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有很有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能把它轉化成我們的建築環境 , 那就有一些令人興奮的潛力在我們建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中運作 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們所想要的複雜性 , 來建造我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築物的運作方式 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要編寫程式的部分 , 可以採取那個序列 , 用它來摺疊或重複 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 使我們能夠從這個程式中解開 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要一些類型錯誤的角度 , 來確保我們成功地建立我們所想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	我要給你們看一些我同事和麻省理工學院的專案計畫 , 在麻省理工學院正在努力達成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	第一兩個是麥克魯機器人和機器人 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模的可重視機器人 , 十二英尺 , 十二英呎長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們用機械電裝裝置 , 感測器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼你想要摺疊成一個序列的角度 , 一個序列的角度 , 0、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一個單位都將它傳送到它的鄰居 , 把它送到鄰居 , 去看它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是聰明的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的會帶來光線:這真的很可怕嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 許多人小時製造這個八呎的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能否真的把這些機械化成每一個部分 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 通過性自然 , 或通過性地嘗試修復程式設計 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它又更進一步 , 試著用實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上是用來計算數位邏輯 , 直接進入你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一個nandgate 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有兩個輸入的鐵路 , 它會讓你運輸 , 而你有兩個輸入鐵 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是使用者的輸入 , 如你所建造的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前面的磚塊開始 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個輸入3d空間 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	意思是 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要磚塊的情況下做些什麼 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算了它在做什麼 , 和你說你想要做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 或下面 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , 1.1 , 輸入平等0 , 輸入 , 結果是下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0.0輸入是1個輸入 , 0.輸入是1輸入 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的資訊被建構出來 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我複製 , 因為你的結構包含了藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入 , 告訴你如何解決這個問題 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些爬行器 , 閱讀它 , 然後把它輸入到其中一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接被嵌入 , 沒有外外的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個項目叫做biaschins , 它可能是最令人興奮的例子 , 就是我們有自動自組系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要重組和系統 , 讓它完全被動系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一個鏈 , 或左派 , 都想要轉右或左邊 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上是編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每一個單位 , 如果它應該轉右或左右 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊成你所編寫的結構 , 例如 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以你基本上可以用三維空間的形狀或維度 , 維持到這個鏈完全完全被動的位置 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來的未來是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 我們的建築物、機器 , 會有新的可能性 , 自我組合、複製、修復 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分中有新的程式能力 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從你有新的可能性來計算 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是很棒的平行和分配計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為這些我剛剛所展示的新技術 , 是一個小步向未來邁進 , 如果我們實施這些新技術 , 一個新的自我組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們登陸月球 , 我們已經到達地球上最深的一點點 , 在海底下一代要去探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探險家納森•沃爾夫提出答案:幾乎所有東西 , 我們都能開始 , 說 , 地球上最深的一點點 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、生物多樣性、探索、微生物學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:我們要探究什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去拜訪了布萊斯康斯康斯康斯康 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我很榮幸 , 二十世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼和雷斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在美國自然歷史博物館中 , 博物館長期以來未知的區域 , 如今 , 阿拉伯沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他真是太棒了 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來 , 他就說 , 印度娜瓊斯特的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在布魯威斯康斯康辛時 , 我給一群中學學生提供了公共演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡要告訴各位 , 如果有比在ted演講中有更嚇人的注意 , 會試著把注意力集成一千個12歲的人 , 一個45分鐘的演講 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在課程結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但有一件事我很困惑 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕的女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該探索什麼 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 很多人有許多人在地球上最深層的探索 , 在地球上 , 他們必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到有意義的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是真的嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	在地球上 , 我們還沒有極大的目標 , 才能探究地球嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我覺得回到我最愛的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁斯•貝吉克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck發現了菸草疾病的成果 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他做的是 , 他把感染的液汁從菸草植物中吸收 , 用過更小的濾器 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到他覺得一定要比最小的生命中所知的細菌更小 , 更小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他提出了一個名字 , 名字是他的謎團 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在未知的病毒中 , 貝莉克真的打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒會在地球上大部分的基因信息 , 比起所有其他生命組合的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然 , 這種世界有很大的實際應用 , 例如 , 避免疫苗的抗爭 , 我們現在知道的主要是由人類的普羅馬病毒組成 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現 , 這不是發生在500年前的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百年前 , 蜜蜂鳥發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有自動飛行器 , 但是我們沒有意識到地球上所有基因資訊的形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	現在我們有了這些奇妙的工具讓我們能夠探討從特定物種的微生物群體的微生物群體 , 讓我們去探索未知的世界 , 像是深度序列 , 讓我們能夠從特殊的物種中尋找基因組 , 不論是哪種類型的微生物 , 都能讓我們去探索未知的環境 , 像是深度序列 , 來記錄所有遺傳資訊 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以應用這些技術從土壤到皮膚 , 到任何東西 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在用一種規定的基準來判斷出爆發的疫情 , 不會造成它們 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓大家了解這個作品如何運作 , 想像一下 , 想像我們從每個人身上拿出一根口味 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常常做的事 , 尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到的是巨大的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到許多人的基因信息 , 大部分是來自於你鼻子裡的細菌和病毒資訊 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了一些非常令人驚訝的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這些資訊時 , 我們會看到大約20%的基因信息 , 你鼻子裡的遺傳信息並不符合我們所見過的基因信息 , 不論是在沒有植物、動物、病毒或細菌之間的遺傳信息 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些數據的小組 , 我們實際上研究這種數據 , 其中一些人已經開始稱之為 「 資訊生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是我們以前所見過的 , 它在我們自己的基因信息中 , 完全不一樣 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為20%的基因信息是生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 大約有40或50%的基因信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對較低的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的信息是暗物質無法被分類或配合我們所見過的東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	首先我們認為也許是人造物品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度的序列工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得越來越精確 , 我們決定信息是生命的一種形式 , 或者至少有些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然假設解釋了生物暗物質的存在 , 只是在它們的生態暗物質中 , 存在著非常令人興奮的可能性:埋藏在這個生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 存在著生命中 , 存在著這種遺傳信息 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索這些弦時 , 基礎上 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命 , 例如 , 基礎 , 改變我們對生物學的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許會讓我們找出癌症的起源 , 或找出我們早期不熟悉的疾病 , 或找出我們所熟悉的新工具 , 或找出疾病的疾病 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 在史丹佛、加州史丹福大學、加州史丹福大學的同事們 , 我們現在正在開啟一個探討生物暗物質 , 來探索生物暗物質 , 來探索生物暗物質 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百多年前 , 人們沒有意識到病毒 , 生命的形式 , 形成了我們地球上大部分的基因信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人類可能完全不知道我們在鼻子裡的新階段 , 可能完全沒有意識到 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	是真的 , 我們可能在地球上發現所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示 , 地球上沒有任何東西 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	威斯康斯康斯康辛 , 他對下一代的探險家提出了很重要的課題 , 像是那位年輕女孩 , 伊吉維斯康斯康 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們把這句話說出來 , 那就像這樣:不假設我們現在認為的 , 其實就是這樣:不假設我們現在在想什麼是全部的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	除非你選擇去探索的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	不知我們周遭的環境 , 都等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	科學家daviddeutsch把理論物理放在回饋上 , 說 , 要承認我們有一個問題 , 要承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技 , 等等 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•迪德在宇宙中所處的宇宙中 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出來 , 說出令人意外的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著做這件事 , 但我想要從兩件事開始 , 大家都知道的 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 大部分的記錄歷史都已知名 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	也就是說 , 地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或任何東西 , 都能維持我們的演化和創造力 , 以至於我們現在存在 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來存活 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有一個很戲劇性的名字:太空船 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	而在太空船外太空船外太空船外太空船 , 宇宙是超級的 , 宇宙是無所不在的 , 我們都仰賴 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們放棄太空船 , 我們就沒辦法去了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都知道 , 人類的歷史 , 人類的歷史 , 其實是不存在的 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如史蒂芬霍金曾說過 , 我們只是一個典型的星球在典型的星系的外星 , 一個典型的星球 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 它在一個典型的星球上 , 繞著一個典型的星球 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的第一句話是:我們在一個典型的地方 , 獨一無二的 , 第二個是說 , 我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩者視為是深刻的真相 , 那麼他們似乎會互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不會阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	第二個問題是:典型的 。 嗯 , 嗯 , 讓我們看看一下 , 一個典型的空間 。 嗯 , 我們看一下 , 一個典型的空間 , 一個典型的空間 , 我們看到牆 , 和化學物質 , 而不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所看到的只有一個藍色的星球 , 如果你遠遠超過一百英里 , 你就會看到太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽系 , 以及恆星 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在銀河系 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	在宇宙中 , 大部分的地方在宇宙中 , 幾乎沒有任何銀河系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再進一步 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時點 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然處於宇宙中一個典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要達到一個典型的地方 , 你必須走到一千倍以外的空間 , 來到一個典型的地方 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子呢 ?
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的宇宙是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	很大的 , ted已經展開了高解析度的虛擬實境空間 , 將來自地質空間的虛擬實境分析 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能否有燈光 , 請 , 我們能看到它嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你看 , 空間中間的空間是完全黑暗的 , 完全漆黑 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	很明顯的 , 當你在那星球上看著最近的星星時 , 你就會看到一個超級新星 , 而那顆星星會被送到你 , 而那顆星星就會被當成超級新星 , 而那顆星星會被送到你 , 而那顆星星是你 , 而那顆星星被打開了 , 直到你 , 你仍然無法看見它的光線 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙的多大和黑暗的宇宙 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管如此 , 光明真是太亮了 , 很明亮 , 非常聰明的事件 , 它會殺死你的石頭在幾光年之內爆炸 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星際空間中 , 遠遠遠離你根本看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	它也非常冷 , 不到三度 , 完全沒有三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	真空是很空的 , 地球上最高的空氣有一百萬倍 , 比我們最高的空氣中最高的空氣 , 真空 , 我們最高的真空可以創造出這個地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是不典型的樣子
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們可以有燈光回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們如何知道一個環境是如此遙遠、外星人 , 和外星人 , 從我們以前的任何東西都一樣 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球的環境 , 我們的形式就是創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 比我們剛剛說的 , 望遠鏡 , 你可以看到它看起來像星星 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們被稱為 「 水龍 」 , 原本的意思是 「 四軸 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	意思是看起來有點像星星 , 但它們不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是幾十億年前、幾十億年前、幾十億年前 , 星系的物質在銀河系崩潰的物質 , 成為超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場會引力崩塌的能量 , 還有一些物質 , 重力崩塌的能量 , 以及一些重力崩潰的能量 , 和我認為它是一兆個太陽的能量 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理不像像物理一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法存活下來 。 語言破壞 , 當試圖描述它的存在時 , 語言就破壞了 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	可能有點像是經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在爆炸時期 , 數百萬年來 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學論壇可以準確地描述、模型、預測 , 並且預測 , 解釋一下 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學論壇可以準確地描述和預測 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了非常精確的模型 , 與其它組合 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是一個超級的圖像 , 它也包含了同樣的數學關係和相同的結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識的知識 。 如果這不夠好 , 信仰是有意義的 , 隨著時間的增長 , 這就是知識的基礎 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理學的物理學有特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那些物理物體 , 不像彼此相同的數學和古老的結構 , 隨時間隨時間地擴張 , 讓它變得更有趣 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們的化學量子是不同的 。 化學的化量是不同的 。 這化學的化量是不同的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構和整體實體世界之間的關係 , 不管是哪個地方 , 都沒有其他地方存在 , 物理世界最重要的東西之一 , 就是它的結構 , 和其它的結構 , 和所有其他地方的關係 , 實際上 , 物理世界的結構和結果 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 我們的形式 , 與我們與宇宙的關係有著相同的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金所說的 , 是真的 , 但它是錯的 。 它是正確的 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是重要的 , 因為知識是資訊處理的過程 , 計算 , 計算 , 計算需要一個電腦 , 不需要一個電腦來計算 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 為了讓媒體在影響上我們發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 更不容易理解 , 解釋是證據 , 是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境是有證據的 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛剛開始測試 , 說 , 牛頓的重力約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但證據顯示我們過去數十億年來一直在不斷地下降 , 每平方公尺的地球數十億年後 , 仍然會持續下降 , 以至於過去數十億年 , 仍然會持續下降 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	如我們所知 , 證據發現最基本的真理 , 證據證明了所有科學領域的所有科學都只是在地球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點是充滿證據的 , 同時也很重要和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星際空間中 , 那些三項最低的可能供應 , 都能提供最低的可能供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它是空的 , 它是冷的 , 它是空的 , 它是冷的 , 它是空的 , 它是冷淡的 , 它是空的 , 很冷 。
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實 , 這只是另一個不可思議的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像一下一個立方體在地面空間中 , 和我們的房子一樣大 , 太陽系的大小 , 正是人類標準的標準 , 但這仍然意味著它包含了超過一百萬噸的重要性 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠 , 說 , 身為一個自我保持的空間站 , 在那裡 , 有一群科學家被投入 , 創造出一種開放式的知識 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 遠遠超越科技甚至將氫氣從二氧化碳排放到其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 實際上 , 在一個不可思議的宇宙中 , 如果不被物理定律所限制 , 那麼 , 有可能阻止我們去做的事 , 那麼 , 有可能阻止我們做的事 , 不是嗎 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識 , 不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動產生能源供應 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應和證據嗎 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再說一次 , 這對人類來說是很明顯的 。 但你要做的是用望遠鏡 , 甚至是日常設計 , 向外望遠 , 看到同樣的銀河系 。
