in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些銀河系中 , 你可以天體物理學物理學 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學 , 等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最難的科學是生物學領域的旅行 , 因為它會花上數億年才能到最遠的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從未做過類似生物學領域的旅程 , 我想我們可以做到每幾億年 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星際空間確實存在於宇宙中的任何一個基礎 , 可以變成相同的狀態 , 如我們所知 , 在宇宙中 , 可以變成相同的狀態 , 如我們所知 , 在宇宙中 , 可以成為我們所謂的 「 知識 」 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是一個獨特的可居住的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果交叉空間可以創造出一個開放式的方案 , 那麼幾乎所有其他環境 。 所以 , 地球是地球 。 所以 , 地球是地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制因素 , 和這裡 , 沒有資源 , 因為它們很有趣 , 還沒有資源 , 因為他們很有智慧 , 還沒有資源 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	關於宇宙的知識 , 我認為應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 ,
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只剩下幾光年 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁最近寫了一本書 , 關於我們脆弱的各種東西 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗錯 , 最重要的是恐怖主義用武器大規模毀滅 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會可以存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他在會議會談到這場演講 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為那是正確的分類 , 來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他說的 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它依賴於不是偶爾 , 而是在我們創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險是無所不在的 。 物種滅絕了 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終止 , 所有物種和所有文明已經存在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	若我們想成為一個存在的特徵 , 我們的特殊關係和物理定律的關係 , 我們就能創造出新的解釋 , 新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 來創造出新的解釋 , 新的知識 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	現在 , 讓我來介紹一下我的意思 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 只是為了說明我所說的內容 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 , 但我不是物理學家 。 根據這個理論 , 我是個物理學家 。 根據這個理論 , 我是物理學家 , 不是正確的物理學家 , 我只是一個層級的物理學家 。 根據這個理論 , 它已經太遲了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們最好的選項就是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 像是kyoto協議 , 及其限制在經濟活動上的限制 , 以及它的限制在經濟活動上 , 最好的選項是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 像是kyoto協議 , 及其限制在經濟活動上的限制 , 以及它的限制在經濟活動上 , 最好的選項是要預防二氧化碳排放 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	投票者的行動 , 甚至還沒辦法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它發生了 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 無法避免它發生了 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代末期 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放會使命運的新冰層消失 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	我看得清楚這一點 , 我不知道為什麼它不是公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	這是我們無法承認的事 。 當我們知道一個臨時的災難時 , 會如何解決它的成本 , 比起災難的代價還要低 , 卻不會有爭議 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 我們還沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個穩定的問題 , 不只是問題的解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	結果是 , 預防治療的預防措施 , 只有我們知道要預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你一直在鼻子上搜索 , 那麼科學醫學不會教導你如何避免懲罰 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學科學停止尋求治癒 , 並專注於預防 , 那它就會變得非常少 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界正在忙碌 , 把氣體排放在所有成本上 , 都能減少 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	應該要在氣候上設計 , 用規劃來降低溫度 , 而不是所有成本都很高 , 但效率很高 。 有些規則 , 例如在空氣中 , 把陽光照亮 , 並鼓勵水平的生物 , 來減少溫度 , 並且在高溫度上 , 沒有任何成本 , 但有效率又便宜 。 還有一些規劃 , 像是在空間中的鏡子 , 來降低溫度 , 並鼓勵水平的生物 , 來減少溫度 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時 , 這些東西都是fring研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類的核心 , 或問題 , 或問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們遇到的問題 , 不僅僅是解決問題 , 而是生存的能力 , 不單是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以 , 拿兩隻石頭 , 把石頭放在他們身上 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一題是: 「 問題是很大的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一方面 , 「 問題是無可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	貧窮困境是如何解決貧窮的問題 ? 經濟學家保羅姆•羅姆提出一個主意: 「 城市 , 城市 , 城市規模的管理區 , 是由國內的規則所組成 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題 , 政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅爾羅馬的主意是:查爾斯的激進想法 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	這對我們來說是個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生正在做自己的家作業 , 因為他們沒有任何電力在家裡 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒有遇過這些特別的學生 , 但是我遇到了這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	咱們來挑選一個例子 , 綠色衣服 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我將tnelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼 , 尼爾森擁有一百歲的科技 , 可以在家裡製造電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	現在 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	壞的規則可以避免這種雙贏的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼規則呢 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個非常低的價格下降低了價格 , 價格低於價格 , 價格低於價格 , 價格低於每單位的價格 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 不管是資源 , 或獎勵 , 都能提供其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看過 , 有一些不同的規則 , 規則 , 商業賺得很大 , 所以他們有一套規則 , 讓商業賺到更好的規則 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這種規則是 , 尼爾森購買他的電話公司的規則 , 都在使用手機公司的規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經看過這些規則如何運作 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變規則 , 用電力來維持現存 , 但從企業和消費者中 , 消費者會想要保存現有的代價 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以 , 他被困住了規則 , 讓他無法讓他贏得解決方案來幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在街道上被困在街道上 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試著找出我們如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們有一些規則 , 可以改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 我們有一個普遍的抽象觀點 , 我們可以做出實踐的選擇 , 在許多國家裡 , 許多國家也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的反對 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領袖的選擇 , 比如給領袖 , 選擇要給領袖的選擇 , 比如給領袖 , 選擇要給領袖的選擇 , 比如給領袖 , 選擇要給領袖的選擇 , 比如給領袖 , 選擇要給領袖的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們想要選擇能夠繼續消費的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一邊或摩擦 , 就會有緊張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法來改變規則 , 會給我們一套規則 , 來改變規則 , 來改變規則 , 來改變規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	nelson也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到破壞規則的圖片 , 規則會讓人們在黑暗中看到 , 例如 , 規則可以讓人們在黑暗中觀察到黑暗的照片 , 例如在黑暗的照片 , 來自美國太空總署的影像 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大放大 , 這裡可以看到北韓 , 像黑洞相比它鄰居的鄰居 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會很驚訝 , 北韓的規則會讓人們在黑暗中看到 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 更深層的了解 , 文化、價值觀和信仰 , 都來自於法律和規定的規則 , 同時也更深層的理解 , 文化、價值觀和信仰 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做出選擇 , 做出選擇 , 導致了非常多樣性的道路 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們能改變人類的規則 , 可以改變我們所習慣的規則 , 更好、更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 在海地 , 在這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也黑暗 , 相較於鄰居的鄰居 , 和其他的鄰居有相同的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	兩個國家都和黑人相比 , 比如海地或多數州長 , 和華盛拉多州的兩者都差不多 , 有半數的居民是海地或墨西哥 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告 , 我們的規則是壞的 , 因為政府是弱的 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只規則是壞的 , 因為政府太強大、壓迫 , 像是北韓 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造環境有好的規則 , 我們就無法撕掉 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們必須找到方法來建立 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大幅展現了潛力和挑戰與規則 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這個圖表上 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人有先前的技術 , 像是鋼、印刷、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用過 , 至少在那段期間 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵傳播這些想法的利潤激動 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快的採用規則 , 慢慢創新 , 把中國從世界各地下降 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 在其他國家 , 創新的國家 , 包括開發新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步中發展出新的規則 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入保持穩定 , 讓世界各地的保持穩定 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是最近的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	中國的平均收入是美國的平均收入 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到它大約有3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在1970年代末期 , 改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的中國開始在中國開始很快地帶著美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到地圖上 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 導致在中國大規模改變的規則 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點 , 你可以看到在上面的邊緣是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是個小小的中國 , 在二十世紀中 , 由英國的規則 , 由英國的規則 , 採用了非常不同的規則 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是個地方有數百萬人可以從土地開始工作像是縫襯衫、製作玩具
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入 , 增加收入的增加 , 越來越多的技能能快速成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典型的模式 , 當他們決定把整個大陸轉向市場模型時 , 他們決定要移動所有的大陸 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但 , 直覺地明白了對他人的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與市場規則 , 沒有任何人在中國轉移到市場規則 , 讓人們可以去工作 , 以某種特殊區塊 , 例如 , 英國的做法是:有機會 , 去市場規則 , 讓所有人都能用市場規則去工作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以 , 他們創造了四個特殊的經濟區塊 , 在那裡 , 中國人可以來到那裡 , 城市成長得很快 , 在那裡 , 城市長大得很快 , 那裡有各個特殊的經濟區塊 , 在那裡 , 中國人可以來和工作 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港的一個城市 , 叫做nzhen 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在這個城市裡 , 有一個塔iphone , 有很多人的公司 , 他們製造了iphone , 由中國人搬到漢堡 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特殊區塊之後 , 有十四個特色區塊 , 在那裡 , 人們可以選擇的優勢 , 他們被打開 , 最終證明成功 , 在這些地方 , 人們可以選擇 , 他們被鎖住了 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	展示成功的成功 , 讓整個經濟體系的成功 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了我們幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存選擇給人們 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:操作正確的規模 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變規則 , 你就能做到 , 但村子的村子太小了 , 你就能做到 , 但村子的數量太小了 , 你能得到好的規則 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會來回顧 , 看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會 , 來看看如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會來回顧 , 看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會來回顧 , 看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會回顧 ,
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會創造新的規則 , 人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	而且它們很大 , 能讓所有受益者 , 只要數百萬人一起在好規則上工作 , 才能得到所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	因此提議是 , 我們有所謂的 「 大城市 」 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一份特定的規劃開始 , 規則要求吸引我們想要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 創造出基礎建設的電力系統 , 道路、運動、機場、港口、機場 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 誰會僱用先前的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你會需要吸引家庭 , 居住在那裡 , 居住永久 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子取得教育 , 並得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	在那裡 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴展這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以再一次地做一次 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它成功 , 我們需要好的規則 , 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些是被捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要選擇給人們 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這實在是建設在不適合居住土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的地點開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新冠軍 , 但沒有人會被迫活下去 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是選擇領導者 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成目標 , 我們想要領導者 , 我們想要領導者 , 我們想要領導者 , 我們想要領導者的需求 , 來協助我們想要領導者的需求 , 來協助我們想要領導者的需求 , 來建立 , 首先在中國和英國合作 , 建立一個小小的市場模型 , 通過中國和英國一起合作 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國很不可思議 , 為了減少世界貧窮 , 而不是我們在過去一世紀中所採取的行動 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這些合作夥伴再次重複 , 我們就能得到全世界各地的益處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 該國會有責任的責任 , 從一個國家轉移到另一個國家 , 讓另一種國家有責任 , 從一個國家轉移到另一個國家的責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 , 但很重要的是 , 當我們開始思考這些東西時 , 可以讓我們拉回來 , 重新思考這些東西 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們拉回來 , 重新思考這些東西 , 才能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們拉回來 , 重新思考這些東西 , 能夠讓我們拉回來 , 重新思考這些東西 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不是殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義最壞的原因是 , 關於殖民主義的議題 , 以及我們對殖民主義的最好處 , 就是它涉及了關於殖民主義的好處 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 包括領導者 , 和那些住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是要阻擋和認知的爭議 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在練習中練習 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們拿一個特定領袖 , 拉克斯特 , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	他必須有機會去做古巴的古巴 , 但他沒有一個香港在古巴 , 那裡有機會去做古巴 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	然而 , 他在南方有一個非常特殊的位置 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	有一塊土地是曼哈頓的一塊土地 , 一塊土地大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	castro去了加拿大的總理 , 說: 「 看 , 黃金是個可怕的問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不加拿大 , 加拿大 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特別的政府區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新的城市被建造出來 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人來到這裡 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	咱們來一個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	一些我的市民也會搬進城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人還會繼續 , 但這將會將現代經濟和現代化的經濟和現代化的經濟和現代化的經濟和現代化的連結 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這種模型在哪裡嘗試呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 , 我和非洲人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	其中許多人都可以選擇成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	規則是改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種創造新的規則的方式 , 讓人們不用反對 , 反而反而對抗氣候變遷 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也能更清楚的承諾 , 如果他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 在一個新的城市裡 , 他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 只要他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們就能做出更可信的承諾 , 在一個新的城市裡 , 他們可以做出更可信的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許甚至有些排列有點像是抽菸帳號 , 你把土地放在帳戶裡 , 和夥伴國家負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有許多土地 , 可以被建造出來 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是一張我在海岸拍攝的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	土地上有巨大的土地 , 像這樣的土地 , 數十萬人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這個想法轉化為數十億個城市 , 甚至數十億個城市 , 會在上世紀有足夠的土地 , 讓它們有足夠的土地嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	在地球上 , 如果我們看著燈光在夜晚 , 它看起來就像世界上大部分都被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我向你們說明為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表所有土地的代表 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	將它轉變成一個平方形 , 代表地球上所有可靠的土地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	這些點代表土地的土地 , 已經超過三十億人口居住的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把底部放到底部 , 就能看到這座城市有三十億個城市居民 , 只佔地球上百分之三十億的城市 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要建造城市數十億人 , 他們就會像這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從3%的土地到4% , 到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅地降低人類足跡在地球上建造更多城市 , 讓人們可以移動 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是由好規則所控制 , 人們有機會得到工作機會 , 擁有機會去工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以用基本的電力來運作 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座城市 , 擴大規模 , 這樣我們就能建造出更多的城市呢 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它會幫助一個人性 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做些細節來寫一些細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不想讓我們逃離城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學術在野生中消失 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你能讓我們思考這個問題 , 假設它不是加拿大的加拿大 , 來處理種族大屠殺 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西是一名參與者 , 或許古巴西也想成為一個夥伴 , 四個共通點都能參與其中 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何作出這樣的治療 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒那麼簡單的 , 但可以輕易地做出來 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何定義這一點 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港是城市 , 製造出大量的價值 , 讓人們開始時 , 都在他們自己所擁有的土地上 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用這塊土地去買東西 , 像是警察、法庭、學校系統 , 以及健康照護系統 , 讓土地更有吸引力 , 讓土地更有吸引力 , 讓土地更有吸引力 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 鼓勵人們幫助建構這個區塊並建立起基礎規則 , 以正確的方向為基礎規則 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多其他細節
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何建造出低成本的成本 , 讓這些建築能有效率的人 , 確保他們安全 , 所以他們不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術的細節都能做到 , 但那些已經開始追蹤這些東西的人 , 已經開始追求這些事情已經開始追求這些東西 , 可能已經開始追求這些事情 , 可能已經開始追求這些東西 , 可能已經開始追求這些東西 , 可能已經開始追蹤這些東西 , 可能已經開始追蹤這些東西 , 可能已經開始追蹤這些事情 , 沒有阻礙 , 沒有阻礙 , 沒有阻礙 , 沒有任何阻礙 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我結論這張照片 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	儘管如此 , 地球上有很多人 , 都是因為我們有這麼多人的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	這不像稀有物品 , 分享的意思是 , 每當我們都少一點點 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都能得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們思考這些想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:規則 , 例如 , 我們的規則是如何互動彼此的規則 , 例如 , 我們有一系列的規則 , 來提供一些知識免費的規則 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	咱們來一個系統 , 在政府辦公室裡 , 有一套系統 , 可以把土地放在政府辦公室裡 , 讓人們可以被排放到政府辦公室裡 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更好 , 所以 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友不需要在街燈上跑步 , 就能繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更好 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學家先生多樣化的基因組成了他的團隊發現了很遠的距離 , 探討了數百萬個基因組成 , 他的研究團隊發現了很遠的速度 , 來談談數百萬個基因組成的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物學 , 生物科技 , 生物學 , 生物學 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna和海裡的頭髮 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	一開始 , 我被問到幾個人關於辯論的辯論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我知道樂觀主義者很悲觀 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我們要如何從讀基因編碼到第一階段 , 開始寫程式碼 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅十年前 , 我們發表了一篇文章 , 發表了第一個序列 , 叫做 「 流感血液 」 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	從13年開始 , 花了13年的時間 , 才完成了4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以做同樣的基因組計畫 , 花兩到八個小時 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	在過去十年 , 大量的基因組成了:人類的基因組 , 包括人類的基因組 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	基因組定序的前幾百年 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組組成序列 , 大約10年前 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組組成 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛剛從gordon和betmordon和betmardon和betridon和貝蒂莫基金會找到了130個基因組 , 由環保生物體系組成 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 究竟到底是什麼 , 我們幾乎沒辦法把地球表面的表面拉出來 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人都不知道 , 因為它們是無形的 , 但微生物只佔據地球生物數量的一半 , 所有動物都只佔據地球生物數量的一半 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人並不常常做的事 , 但如果你把海水帶到海裡 , 你就會吞下海水 , 記住每一百萬個細菌 , 每一千萬隻病毒就有一百萬隻細菌 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到5000種微生物物種被排列在兩年前 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了第二次的探險計畫 , 嘗試樣本海洋的海景 , 每200英里以外的樣本 , 拍攝海洋景象 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在巴拿馬的加勒比海海岸 , 加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海等等 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱辛的 , 我們在一艘船上做這件旅行 , 讓年輕人了解科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們採取海水 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們的實驗室 , 在岩維爾 , 我們收集不同的濾水 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們的實驗室 , 在岩維爾 , 我們收集不同的濾水 , 然後把它們的dna帶回實驗室在岩維爾 , 我們每24小時就可以排列出一億個字母 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	這麼做 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 認為我們眼睛中的視覺色素 , 只有一個或兩個有機體在環境中 , 都有相同的顏色 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有物種都在海洋的溫暖區域中 , 用陽光來源 , 利用太陽光來源於它們的能量和溝通 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 我們發現了1.3萬個新的基因 , 還有許多五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經把這張照片從sloan基金會的椅子上賣出來了 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量了多少病毒和細菌所有我們每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機或閉上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	透過一些簡單的應用程式 , 我們收集了數十億微生物 , 僅僅僅僅在紐約市的一棟大樓上 , 收集數十億微生物 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們現在正處於序列的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	在資料集中 , 在資料集中 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋中發現幾乎每兩百英里 , 都會看到巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	在不同的溫度上 , 不同的溫度會降低 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 由溫度降低溫度 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 , 我們發現有很大的差異在溫度的紅色溫度 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是低溫的 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一件令人驚訝的是這些光的光波長度可以預測 , 根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測基礎 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	從區域到區域 , 都很有偏見 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外 , 在深海裡 , 最藍色的光源是藍色的 , 光是藍色的 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	那裡有許多綠光 , 就會看到很多綠色的光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們更有可能在極端中移動到紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了嘗試 , 了解我們基因的基因資料 , 我們組合所有資料 , 包括我們全部的基因資料 , 將所有的資料包含在地球上 , 超過一半的基因資料包含了全部的基因資料 , 包含了我們全部的基因資料 , 將所有資料包含在地球上 , 超過一半的基因資料 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些發現新的家庭 , 看看這些發現:我們發現了新的家庭 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每種新樣本 , 我們都在對這些新家庭做些新樣本 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	因此 , 我們在這個星球上最早的階段發現了基本的基因、組成和生命 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們觀察所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角和動物 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約290萬個基因組中 , 我們只有大約2萬6千個基因 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物聚集在一起 , 我們可能會分享不到三萬個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因不僅是演化的設計演化 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在基因組合中 , 基因組合的不同組合 , 會導致這些基因組成的不同結構 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna組成dna序列的能力在過去十年或兩年間 , 已經改變了 , 相同的dna序列在過去十年或兩年間 , 已經改變了 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組 , 在1995年 , 基因組合成基因組合成基因組 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 說: 「 我心我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	hemophilus有一千八百個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 500 , 另一個500 , 一個比較小的基因會產生最小的組合嗎 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做轉變性突破 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	翻譯只是小小的dna , 隨機在基因編碼中的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果在基因的中間 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 所有基因都可以採取轉移 , 我們稱之為 「 沒有基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境是非常關鍵的 , 而你只能定義一個基本或不必要的基因基礎 , 只能定義一個基本或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智慧方法 , 和13個相關器官的基因組進行比較 , 我們試著用更直接的智慧方法 , 來找出他們共有的狀況 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	而我們發現只有173個基因 , 只有173個基因 , 只有173個基因 , 都是13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	一旦我們忽略細胞寄生蟲 , 它就擴張了 , 如果我們忽略了一顆細胞寄生蟲 , 它擴張了大約310個基因的位置 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴張或收縮基因組 , 根據你的觀點來看 , 可能300到400個基因組 , 依據你的觀點 , 大約300到400個基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法是要建構一個人造染色體 , 並且我們必須用這種方式來建立一個人造染色體 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現合成精確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆•史密斯、我同事們 , 開發了一種令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們能合成5 , 000個鹼基對 , 只有兩週期內 , 只有兩週期內 , 只有一個兩週期 , 它的序列和生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個非常令人振奮的實驗 , 我們採用了病毒粒子的基因組成dna , 然後殺死細菌 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一批合成病毒的病毒 , 早已被做成病毒 , 但只有十分之一 , 才有三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這種軟體現在正在製造它自己的硬體 , 而這也是我們和生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻開始評估這個區域 , 我最近在參議院委員會委員會議員 , 和委員會議員 , 特別委員會委員會 , 委員會在參議院委員會委員會議員 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實變得更重要 , 要讓現實發生 , 和人們的想像力 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何病毒都是由基因組組成的 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就會想到伊波拉或小東西 , 但dna從這個器官沒有感染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造了小型生物基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的關心安全部門是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯盟 , 都在嘗試創造生物戰法 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那研究真的被關閉 , 不該有很小的活動 , 就能讓設計師病毒在未來 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內就可能存在 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	即便是可能性細胞 , 在十年內 , 我們就有可能存在 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在已經製造了幾十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以把卡塞特和基因放進這個人造染色體中 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把所有其他人都放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一組合理的組合系統 , 將這些碎片放到染色體中 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是來自生物體內的輻射線 , 可以將三百萬種輻射輻射 , 沒有被殺害 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它的基因組合成了它的染色體 , 在它的染色體中 , 大約12至24小時 , 染色體已經被爆炸了 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上很普遍 , 可能在外太空中 , 存在於我們的旅行中 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	在大約一半一百萬輻射的輻射中 , 一個玻璃碎片 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和破裂 , 當微生物坐在底部時 , 會變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一個實際的圖片:這張圖顯示了基因組 , 一百七十萬種罕見的輻射 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體是完全散散的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是同一個dna自動組裝在24小時後 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人驚訝的是這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有千萬種不同的物種 , 可能有數以千計的物種 , 可能沒有成千上萬種不同的物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成之後 , 第一步就是把它們轉移到細胞沒有基因組合成的細胞 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅能了解生物學的基礎 , 還能帶來巨大的潛力 , 不只是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還能帶來巨大的潛力 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 來自於我們所序列的二氧化碳 , 它的能量來源是氫氣 , 它的能量來源是氫 , 它的能量源自於二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以 , 我們知道很多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 可以捕捉回來的 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 用碳從大氣中抽取出來 , 用碳來從大氣中吸收 , 將它從大氣中轉換成生物聚合物 , 或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種有機體存在於碳氫和氧氣中 , 而我們用的是減少能量來製造氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 也有許多道路可以用來製造甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一項主要的計劃 , 用來捕捉並將甲烷從氣體中 , 變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短期內 , 我認為 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來創造出一百萬個不同的染色體基因組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來創造一百萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學 , 你可以選擇通過篩選 , 不論你是否被篩選出來 , 包括氫化物 , 或化學產品 , 或任何生物學 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的角色 , 就會變得更好 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試修改光合作用 , 來製造氫氣直接從陽光升起 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用氧氣 , 我們有氧氣濃度的氫氣 , 我們認為它會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了細胞製造乙醇的酵素 , 製造乙醇的酵素 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖和酵素 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在大型實驗室使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化學成分比我們最好的化學家製造出的化學還要複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的源源 , 希望是食物的源源 , 希望能是食物的源源 , 希望能是食物的源源 , 希望能是食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源頭 , 希望能成為食物的源頭 , 希望能成為食物的源源 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用道德和政策研究做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們從1999年開始進行實驗 , 直到我們完成一個人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要宗教都參與這個 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為這些宗教領袖用他們的文字寫作法律書 , 沒有任何東西可以做這些實驗 , 因爲我們在做這些實驗時 , 才會發現他們在做的事 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會已經資助了一系列的規則 , 科學團隊的規則 , 像我自己應該在這個區域進行的 , 我們試著為我們建立好的例子 , 來做好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了對恐怖生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們很簡單的議題 , 我們能設計些東西來製造乾淨能源 , 也許革命化開發中國家能提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說幸福和未來 , 他建議我們將我們的直覺轉換為第一步 , 來改善我們的人生 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦 , 企業 , 快樂 , 心靈 , 心理學 , 科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo預設了一個健康 。

life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是充滿誘惑的 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 再來 , 反思 , 爭論 , 反思 , 爭論 , 和未來的焦點和焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會落入熱情之中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年女孩 , 被性愛的誘惑 , 直到婚姻 , 感謝你喬治了大量的百分之六十 , 並且在一年內被排除 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都沒有使用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	承諾要承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們嘗試四歲孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	牠們有一顆棉花糖 , 但是如果他們等到實驗者回來時 , 他們就可以有兩個 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等等 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩童都在誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 之後再來 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	史丹佛大學的同事在史丹福大學的同事在史丹福大學了14年後 , 試著找出與這些孩子有什麼不同的地方 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	孩子們有很大的差異 , 在許多方面 , 都有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	救贖了250位的孩童 , 保存了250點 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像是一組不同的智商標準 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒多麻煩 。 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且決心的關鍵 , 我今天的關鍵是 , 你的關鍵是 , 他們是未來的 , 而不是現在的鑰匙 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間是怎樣的呢 ? 這就是我今天要談的內容 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	觀點是人類體驗的研究 , 或時間分裂 , 或時間分裂 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動和無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化、國家之間、社會階級之間 , 和社會階級之間的差距 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 牠們會變得偏見 , 因為你學會會被偏見 , 因為你學會會變得偏見 。
what determines any decision you make ?	什麼決定你做出決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出一個決定 , 你要做出一個決定 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對於某些人來說 , 其他人正在做的事 , 以及你所感受到的 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們做出決策時 , 我們會稱之為 「 自願者 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現況是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是說: 「 我過去所經歷過的情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	他們的決策是基於過去記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會把這些人稱為 「 過去原始人 」 , 因為他們專注在哪裡 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對於其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在 , 而是在未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來期望 」 , 他們專注於未來的期望 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要辯論 , 時間悖論 , 反而是影響你所做出的每一個決定 , 你完全沒有意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	意思是 , 你有這種偏見的觀點 , 就會有這種偏見 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 , 其中有兩種方式 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	過去有兩種方式 , 未來有兩種方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以專注於正面或負面的負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以被掌控 , 專注在喜悅生命中 , 或虛擬主義者 , 它並不重要 , 你的生活被控制 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以成為未來的目標 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或你是超越未來的: 「 生命早在死亡後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理的靈活性 , 可以改變時間觀點 , 轉換時間觀點 , 其實是你必須學習的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快的 , 最佳的時代是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	很高 , 很高 , 未來很高 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代化的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於過去負面和真實主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最樂觀的臨界是你從過去所傳遞到的 , 你把你的家人、身分和你的家人、身分和你的個人連結在一起 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來的目的就是要追求新的挑戰 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現場表達出來的能量是能量 , 去探索自己、人、人、感知 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間的觀點 , 都比正面更有負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來犧牲成功的原因是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲家庭時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲個人的優勢 , 犧牲個人的婚姻 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲睡眠 , 所以它會影響健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活著工作、成就 , 以及控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我肯定和一些tedsterstersterstersterster 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我是南布朗克斯區的一個貧窮的孩子 。 一個貧窮的孩子 , 在南布朗克斯區的一個貧窮的孩子 , 也是在南布朗克斯區的貧民窟 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我是位在前面的那些犧牲者 , 做這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入我 , 讓我成為未來的主人 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那棉花糖 , 因為如果你等待你會得到兩位 , 直到我學到平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了專注在過去的正面上 , 我比過去更有創意 , 更有生產力 , 而且我比以前更高興 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想要說 , 我們正在應用這個世界問題:改變許多問題:改善家庭衝突 , 例如:改善貧民區 , 改善家庭衝突 , 例如:改善貧民區 , 改善家庭衝突 , 例如 「 增加五百分之一 」 , 持續和保育 , 來改善貧民窟 , 改善貧窮的環境 , 改善家庭衝突 , 例如 , 改善家庭衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是 , 許多人生的謎題都可以透過理解你的時間觀點和其他人的理解 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果是非常深遠的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今有多少人的頭條新聞報導 , 「 長期新聞 」 計畫收集了這些故事 , 不只重要 , 但在2010年時 , 他提高了近期的頭條新聞 , 關於 「 長期新聞 」 這個計畫收集了數十年 , 甚至數十年來 , 甚至在ted2010年 , 他高速地將近期的頭條新聞寫成 「 長期新聞 」 計畫收集故事 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學 。

it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是由tedsterster所建立的 , 由tedsterster包括kevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkevinkelly和stewart品牌 。

so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我將要集中最令人興奮的故事之一 , 過去兩年半 , 我們在土星的大型探險旅程中進行了這次大探險的探險 。

and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是一種身體 , 它有很長的感染人 , 看過地球的行星 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常大 , 實際上 , 它的表面環境被認為更像我們在地球上的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 沒有任何其他的身體在地球上 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層是大氣層 , 像是甲烷、乙烷 , 大氣層 , 大氣層是大氣層 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在泰坦的大氣層中被破壞了 , 他們的產品會加入混合在一起 , 使它們的冷藏起來 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這隻海豹是無所不在的 , 它完全是全球性的 , 全是全國性的 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你無法在眼睛看到的表面 , 眼睛的視覺區分 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但是這些微粒子 , 經過數十億年 , 直到地面 , 被壓縮到表面上 , 經過數十億年的溫度 , 直到表面 , 被壓縮到表面上 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以就像是平均、油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們所懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別甲烷和乙烷 , 這些分子特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 這些分子特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 這些分子特別是甲烷和乙烷 。 這些分子特別是甲烷和乙烷 。 這些分子特別是甲烷和乙烷 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是泰坦水在地球上 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	在大氣層中 , 這樣的情況是可以產生的 , 那些雲層 , 可以有數百公里的空氣 , 來避免任何陽光從水面上升起 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是350度 , 表面的溫度是攝氏350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管如此寒冷 , 你可能會降落在土衛六的表面上 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在地球上 , 它會形成河流和水晶 , 它可以創造峽谷 , 它能形成河流和水晶 , 它能創造峽谷 , 它能形成河流和水晶 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以從高山山脈和山丘下降到低地 , 這樣停下來想想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像一下土衛六的表面 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 , 在泰坦的黑暗是暗的 , 高速在地球上是黑暗的 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很冷 , 可能是雨林 , 你可能會站在雷克密西根湖密西根州的湖密西根湖岸 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在titan的表面上看到的 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在titan的表面上發現了 , 雖然它不是一樣細節 , 細節的描述也很有趣 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 它就像是卡西尼人 , 它就像是卡西尼人 , 一直以來 , 像克斯丁尼一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如同我所說的 , 它有厚厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是泰坦的照片 , 由太陽的背景拍攝 , 背景是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球 , 我不知道它是哪一個 , 它是非常強大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有樂器在卡西尼號的儀器上 , 可以從大氣層中看到 , 我的攝影機系統是其中之一 。
