and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮和黑暗的區域 , 這對我們來說是很明顯的 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	非常神秘:我們無法在泰坦看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域 , 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 實際上 , 這裡是一塊土地的表面 , 但在土地的表面上有一些很小的表面 , 其實是很小的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	這裡有一些特徵 , 看起來是圓形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來像是被分開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到任何線條 , 就會表示有一段碎形 , 就像是錯的 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以 , 它一直是直接的改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但是我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到六個月後 , 我們進入軌道上 , 一個事件發生了 , 被稱為 「 卡斯納尼號調查 」 的調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	由於地球表面 , 由於土衛二的大氣層 , 由於土衛六年 , 在太陽系中 , 我們將它送到大氣層 , 用在土衛六 , 將它送到大氣層 , 用在土衛二 , 花了兩半半小時 , 才能將它放到大氣層 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調一下 , 這到底是多麼重要的 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人造的裝置 , 它在太陽系中第一次在人類史上第一次出現 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	很明顯的是 , 在我的腦海裡 , 整個美國和歐洲的事件都很明顯 , 這種事件 , 應該被慶祝在美國和歐洲 , 悲慘的事件 , 並不是這樣 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很有意義 。 這是個國際性的任務 , 在德國的演講中 , 首先 , ted的演說會出現在英語中 , 美國的口音 , 還有德國人 , 尤其是英國的國會 , 英國口音和英語音響 , 以及美國的口音 , 還有德國人 , 在德國 , 特別是國際任務 。 這是一個國際任務 。 這是一個國際的任務 , 在德國 , 首先 , 和德國的日常一樣 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是個關於 「 聯合國 」 的概念 , 一個真正的聯合國集結在一起 , 成為一個真正的聯合國集合在一起 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要去探索一個行星 , 一個行星的系統 , 人類已經不可置信了 , 直到現在人類真的碰到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我會說 , 要花點時間去談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	這真的是件令人感激的事件 , 也是我個人永遠不會忘記的 , 而你也不應該這麼做 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但無論如何 , 探測器在下面進行測量 , 並且也拍攝了大氣層的照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴你們 , 看到的第一張圖片是從探測器上拍出來的 , 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這很震驚 , 因為我們所想要的其他照片從軌道上移動 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是個不可思議的模式 , 一個邏輯模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一個可以形式的液體 , 可以用液態來形成的 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些頻道 , 可以觀察它們的頻道 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們將這條線帶到這個區塊 , 在那裡 , 進入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你正在看著海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的流體嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像是海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是16公里 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是8公里的照片 , 又一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里 , 大概是飛行的飛行器 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你將飛機在美國的飛機上飛行 , 你就會在這些高度上飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在泰坦尼亞航空飛行的窗戶外面的照片 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 在外太陽系的表面上 , 我將展示給各位看 , 先生女士 , 先生們 , 首先是來自太陽系外太陽系的表面 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰泡 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它在一個平面的黑暗區域中被扭曲 , 而它不會被忽視 。 所以它不是液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	原來的底部是泥巴 , 基本上就是泥巴 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是個不可思議的地面 , 裡面有液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這種材料被廢棄的土地 , 在我們所看到的這些頻道上 , 數十億年來填滿在低水底下的土地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是 「 獵原原本 」 的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 我們的影像中沒有標記 , 甚至是大型的液體的影像 , 或甚至是液體的影像 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	牠們在哪裡呢 ? 更令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛二的一百公尺高的地點 , 他們會在土地上飛行 , 挖掘出這些沙丘 , 它們是一百公尺高 , 距離數公里 , 遠距離距離距離 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	大約有1000或1 , 000或1 , 000或1 , 000或1200英里 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是撒哈拉沙漠的沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很明顯地 , 一個地方很乾燥 , 或你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 難以置信 , 直到最後 , 我們看到湖泊在北極區域 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	南極地區有個湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	差不多是湖泊塔里奧的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 一週一半前 , 我們飛過北極點 , 再次發現 , 我們在海底的特徵上發現了一件事 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎是液體 , 有些原因我們不了解 , 或至少這季節時 , 很明顯地在海森 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	大家會同意我們發現泰坦是個很奇妙的星球 , 但奇怪的是地球本身 , 像地球一樣 , 地球本身 , 和豐富的星球 , 地球本身 , 和豐富的地球 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們回到土衛二 , 這裡是泰坦的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 只是你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常明顯的 , 它的表面很明顯地被破壞了 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是非常地理性的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在埃斯蘭德斯的母親發現 , 我們在南極找到了這個系統 , 我們在南極找到了這個系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的顏色 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋 , 這些碎片被包含有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個區域 , 南極區域 , 整個區域 , 溫度是地球上最高的溫度 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 地球的熱帶比熱帶還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拿出更多的圖片時 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片中 , 冰粒會擴展到太空中 , 數百英里外 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把顏色的影像帶出光線時 , 我們看到這些噴射噴射出光層 , 我們看到這些噴射的光源在土地上數千英里外 , 進入太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我的團隊和我研究了一些類似這樣的圖像 , 像這樣 , 像這樣 , 想出了其他的結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到了結論 , 這些噴泉可能是從土壤中噴出的液態水 , 在土地表面 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有有機物質、有機物質 , 和過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能有有機體的環境 , 可以適應生活有機體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們我們太陽系裡的發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學上的發現 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明 , 基因已經發生了 , 不只一次 , 同時 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 根據我們的太陽系 , 它已經發生了很多次 , 發生在宇宙的三十七十億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	現在 , 地球是唯一的星球 , 我們仍然知道 , 地球是唯一的星球 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 目前我們所知的唯一一個家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們在1968年被阿波羅八號太空人所拍攝 , 那麼你會記得這個非常有名的照片 , 由阿波羅8號太空人拍攝的 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是第一次地球從太空中拍攝 , 它對我們對地球的重大影響在宇宙中 , 以及我們對地球的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在casini拍攝了一場前所未見的照片 , 人類眼睛也看不到 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的一面 , 來自土星的一面 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張照片中 , 你看到了太陽的重覆 , 實際上 , 由於太陽的光線 , 你看到了太陽的背景 , 實際上 , 由於土衛二 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這張美麗的影像 , 我們還不夠聰明 , 我們就能在土星的影像中 , 看到我們自己的星球 , 由土星在土星的衛星拍攝 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些深刻的看法 , 看著我們自己的小小、藍色的星球在其他世界的天空中 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們所知的觀點 , 從這段旅程發現的一半個世紀前 , 我們從這趟旅程發現了一半個世紀 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	2005年 , 只有15%的人在這個短期內 , 發現世界各地的地圖和未知道路 。 這段短期的演講 , 谷歌的結尾 , 叫做 " 谷歌 " 的 " 地圖 " , 在這短期內 , 全球的地圖製造者 , 使用地圖繪製工具 , 全球各地的人都在使用地圖 , 來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、技術 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉里斯坦•卡爾加達:製作地圖對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 塞羅尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人都需要幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人民和供應給當地 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有任何地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地圖會被大量地描繪出來 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國在世界各地的地圖上有許多問題:沒有細節的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40位志工用一個新的軟體來繪製一萬三千公里的路、三千個醫院、邏輯和信息 。
and it took them four days .	花了四天 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體嗎 ? google地圖製造 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	google地圖是一套科技 , 讓每個人都能在地圖上我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有從路上傳送到商店的路線 , 從路到街道 , 到商店 , 到街區 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎得主 , 諾貝爾獎得主 , 諾貝爾獎得主張地 , 大部分開發中國家 , 都要把大量的未經營地帶給大量 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 一兆美元的土地產量 , 沒有在印度獨立 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	去年 , 上千個使用者在170個國家收集了數以千計的資料 , 創造出一張地圖 , 完全不明確的地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	由於熱情使用者的力量 , 每一層都可以使用 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	咱們來看看一些地圖是由使用者所創造的 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 當我們說話時 , 人們正在繪製世界 , 在170個國家中 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑在塞內加爾的橋樑 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	更接近家鄉 , 盧安 , 加羅拉在孟加拉 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這就是計算幾何學的結果 , 機器學習 , 以及機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以百計的城市 , 一個使用者 , 一個使用者 , 一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這個邀請給我們地球上百分之七十的受邀 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴西亞的巴西人問了為什麼我們只關注暴力抗議 , 阻止阻止障礙而非暴力的抗議阻止障礙 , 去阻止阻止障礙 , 而非暴力抗議 , 阻止阻止障礙而非暴力抗議 , 阻止阻止障礙 , 而不是那些非暴力的領袖 , 可以和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞:注意非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	在過去的8年裡 , 我已經把我的人生記錄為以色列和巴勒斯坦人試圖結束衝突和平的權利 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:那是巴勒斯坦甘地嗎 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所聽到的問題之一是 , 通常我剛從中東 , 我從中東拍攝數十個巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 用非暴力來防護他們的土地和水資源 , 用非暴力來防護他們的土地和水資源 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正在嘗試 , 讓大規模的國家非暴力運動最終佔領並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分人可能都從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這裡發生在地面和平的抗爭運動中 , 發生了什麼事 , 和平的抗爭是其中一個關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來談談注意力的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及在西非暴力運動的力量 , 加薩和其他地方 , 但我現在的研究是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大規模的非暴力行為 , 不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力 , 但為了我們開始關注這些人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我說明一下這個村莊 , 叫布德魯斯的村莊 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣布 , 會建造一個隔離障礙 , 而在這座村莊的一部分 , 會建造一個隔離障礙 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地和被周圍 , 所以他們失去了40%的土地並被周圍 , 所以他們失去了40%的土地並被周圍圍繞 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過鼓舞當地領導力 , 他們發起了一個和平的抗議活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 讓你可以感覺一下 , 在地面上看起來是怎麼樣的 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦婦女:我們被告知牆會分開巴勒斯坦的女人 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布魯斯 , 我們意識到牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人來說 , 事實上 , 創造了一個解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男人:今天你受邀到一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十名以色列兄弟姐妹所加入的 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列行動主義者:比非暴力反對的軍隊更不暴力 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試圖推出軍人 , 但沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	fatah黨員:我們必須擁抱我們的傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈瑪斯派對:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想要把它帶到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	協調:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	fatah , 哈馬斯和普遍的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞報導: 「 沿著管子持續下去 。 」
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去散播人群 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活著的彈子 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像布拉威 , 每次都在拍攝 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列行動主義者:我肯定我們都死了 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身上 , 也有其他人 , 甚至還沒關心 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止它 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	主持人:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	沒有需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	聊天:我們能做到 ! 我們能做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴基:當我第一次聽到關於布德魯斯的故事 , 我很驚訝 , 在2003年 , 國際媒體已經失敗了 , 到布德魯斯的事件發生了很大的事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 數十個月後 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦之間 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦之間的區分 , 以以色列和巴勒斯坦之間的區分 , 以色列與巴勒斯坦之間的距離 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	巴勒斯坦的社區在耶路撒冷的抗爭中 , 巴勒斯坦的社區在耶路撒冷 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然對這些故事感到沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會造成深刻的後果 , 不管在巴勒斯坦有沒有暴力的可能性 , 或甚至存活在巴勒斯坦 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗拒和非暴力抗爭 , 都是一種戲劇的形式 , 讓觀眾能對他們造成的影響 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力的演員是唯一一個能夠成功的機會 , 讓非暴力的政策者 , 會變得非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 , 會對巴勒斯坦問題感到非常困難 , 沒有暴力的領導者會讓他們在巴勒斯坦的議題上變得非常困難 , 不讓非暴力者 , 會變成非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 , 會讓它變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 會讓它變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 會讓它們的團體變成非常困難的非暴力者 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的注意力可能會在房間裡不陌生 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓孩子變得更大膽 , 要讓孩子變得更大 , 讓孩子變得更大膽 , 讓孩子變得更大 , 讓孩子變得更大 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	童年心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經學會兒童心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道他能得到父母的關注 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以鼓勵或把注意力放在他們的孩子身上 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區的行為和國家都可以受到影響 , 依靠國際社群選擇聚焦注意力 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在中東和平 , 要讓非暴力的領導者能夠改變非暴力行為 , 讓非暴力行為更加關注到現今的非暴力行為 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在加薩和東耶路撒冷的村莊裡 , 我看到了影響 , 甚至一部紀錄片能影響到它的轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉威的村落裡 , 社區正面臨著非常類似的波拉布德魯士 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去了許多土地 , 沒有自由取得權利 , 像是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們一直在使用非暴力行為 , 兩年來 , 但從沒人注意到 , 他們已經開始使用非暴力 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們會說出最好的示範 , 和現代的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們在電影裡看到了布達德魯斯的文件 , 認為 , 人們會追蹤他們在做的事 , 人們會關心 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	以色列為索利亞里特 , 這位是伊斯蘭國的新和平運動 , 叫做孤立 , 和平運動叫做slidariot , 代表團結團結合 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這種運動的領導者已經使用布德魯士 , 作為他們主要的指導工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導了非暴力人士開始加入他們的活動 , 了解非暴力的力量開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	巴哈和伊斯蘭德的例子 , 即便是獨立電影可以扮演一個角色 , 改變非暴力行為 , 變成一個功能行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 媒體玩家的力量會變得更明顯、有價值觀、有效率 , 並在他們的作品中 , 比如伊斯蘭、巴爾斯坦、伊斯蘭、巴爾斯坦 , 伊斯蘭國的非暴力領導者會變得更明顯、更有價值 , 且有效果 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事情是要了解如果我們不關注這些努力 , 他們就隱形了 , 就像他們從未發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但 , 我先舉手 , 若我們這麼做 , 他們會多重 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們多大 , 他們的影響會成長在巴勒斯坦的衝突中 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力可以終於阻擋這個情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導者證明非暴力工作就像布德魯斯一樣 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	咱們來讓他們注意力 , 讓他們能證明它在任何地方都能成功 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙沙克有個很簡單又強大的模型 , 鼓舞人心的領導力 , 包括蘋果、馬丁•路德金、馬丁•路德•金恩 , 和他的例子 , 包括蘋果、馬丁路德金、馬丁路德金 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	貝殼、商業、企業、領導力、銷售、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•沙克:偉大的領導者鼓舞人心 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不像我們假設的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者 , 更好的是 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能夠達成這些東西時 , 似乎都無法達成什麼樣的感覺 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	舉例來說 , 為什麼蘋果這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年後 , 一年後 , 他們比所有競爭都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一台電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的能力 , 相同的資料 , 同一間公司 , 同一家公司 , 同一部公司 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德•金恩領民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一的美國人 , 他肯定不是唯一的受害者 , 而他肯定不是唯一的男人 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼 , 萊特兄弟可以找出控制權力 , 控制權力的人 , 在某些其他的團隊中 , 更好的資金是: 「 權力飛行 。 」
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有成人飛行 , 萊兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的方式 , 甚至深深地改變了我的觀點 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 所有偉大且鼓舞人心的領袖和組織 , 不管是蘋果或馬丁路德金 , 或是馬丁路德•金恩或馬丁路德金 , 他們都認為 , 行為和溝通的方式 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全相反對其他人 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是把這個世界最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼樣 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠鼓舞其他人 , 卻沒有 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我定義一下很快的說法 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上的每一個組織 , 都知道他們所做的 , 或100% 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你是否稱它為 「 不論你是否稱之為你的分配式的價值觀點 , 或你所謂的不論你是如何運作的 。 」
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但 , 非常少人或組織知道他們為何做這些事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	由於 「 為什麼 」 我並不表示 「 為何 」 做利益 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果的結果 , 結果總是會結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的信念是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼每個人都關心 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們的思考方式 , 我們的行為方式 , 溝通的方式是從外面來 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯的 , 我們從最明顯的事物中從最明顯的到最明顯的地方 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵領袖和鼓舞人士 , 不管他們的產業 , 都認為 , 和鼓舞的組織 , 不管他們的產業 , 都認為 , 和鼓舞的組織 , 不管他們的產業都一樣 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都得到它 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 會聽到這樣的聲音: 「 我們做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們是美麗的設計 , 簡單使用和使用者 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? " 啊 ! "
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這是多數的銷售量 , 最重要的是 , 銷售量是如此 , 最多人是這樣做的 , 大部分人都這樣做 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說 , 我們怎麼做 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說 , 我們是怎麼做的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說 , 我們是怎樣的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說我們是怎麼做的 , 或如何做得更好 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師 , 最好的律師 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做事業 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有較高的氣體 , 可以有較高的氣體 , 也有更好的氣體 , 可以有更好的氣體 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這就是蘋果的溝通方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現況 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思維 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品美麗設計、簡單使用和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛剛做好的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同 。 你準備好要買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是逆轉這些資訊的秩序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它證明我們是人們不買你做的事 , 人們買了你做的事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了你做的事 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋為何在這個房間裡的每個人都非常舒服購買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但是我們也非常舒適地購買一個來自蘋果電腦的手機 , 或來自蘋果的手機 , 或是來自蘋果的手機 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如同我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一台電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何一個競爭對手的競爭 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者完全同樣品質化製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 高速公路發出了flatvs 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有用平面的螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	幾年來 , 他們都在製作平面螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾出了3個玩家和pdas , 他們做了很棒的品質產品 , 他們做出很好的品質產品 , 且他們做出完美的產品 , 卻沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像購買一個mp3球員 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買一台電腦公司的一台電腦公司 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了你做的事 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標並不是要和所有需要你有的人做事業 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你相信的人做事業 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最好的部分:我沒有告訴你們我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	它是生物學的基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一下人類的大腦 , 從頭部看 , 你看到的就是人類大腦實際上被破碎成三個主要的零件 , 和黃金圓圈一樣 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新大腦 ,
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析思想和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個區塊會讓我們的大腦負責 , 我們的肢體大腦負責所有我們的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責人類行為、決策 , 且沒有能力語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面交流時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、有利、事實和事實 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們從內部交流 , 我們會直接告訴大腦控制行為的一部分 , 然後讓人們可以用我們所說的做法和做法來處理行為 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道所做的決定 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給人一些事實和細節 , 說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節 , 都說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說 , 但它並不感覺 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會使用這種動詞 , 不會覺得 「 感覺 」 是的 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦的一部分 , 控制語言並不控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的辦法是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不好 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	有時你會說你是你的心臟 , 或是你會帶領你的心靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭去打破你們 , 那些不是其他身體的部分控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都在你的肢體大腦中 , 大腦控制決策和非語言的大腦 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你做這樣的事 , 而人們會去投票給你 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再次 , 目標不僅僅是賣給那些需要你的人 , 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不僅僅是雇用工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 你知道的 , 如果你僱用那些相信你相信的人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用那些相信你所相信的人 , 他們會為你工作 , 為你的錢而戰 , 但如果你雇用人 , 他們會為你的錢而工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	另外還有一個更好的例子 , 比萊兄弟更好 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在二十世紀初期 , 電力飛行者的追求力力飛行就像是今日的旅行 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試它 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley , 我們假設的 , 是成功的基礎 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 甚至現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三件事:受試者、錯人、壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	一直都是相同的三件事 , 讓我們來探索 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley已經5萬美金 , 把這台飛機運送了 。
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在smithsmithsmithsmithsmithsmithsmithsmithsmithsonian工作 , 他知道所有偉大的思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的心智金錢可以找到和市場條件很棒
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報追蹤了他 , 每個地方都有人 , 都是根深蒂固 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	我們從來沒有聽過samuelpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠 , 在華盛頓俄亥俄州 , 俄亥俄州 , 俄亥俄州 , 我們認為是成功的基礎 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 他們付錢給他們的夢想 , 來自自行車店 ; 而紐約時報 , 沒有一個人在萊布羅大學的教育 , 不管是波爾堡 , 還沒有錢 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差異是 , 維爾和威爾巴爾是由一個信念所驅動的 , 由於一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能找出這個飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的一面 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要有錢 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追尋結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富裕 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	瞧瞧 , 發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想與他們有血液、汗水和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則是為了支票而做 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說 , 每次萊兄弟出去時 , 他們就要花五個組件 , 因為那就是他們花了五組成就 , 因為那就是他們要花五個組成的部分 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 在12月17日1903年12月17日 , 萊兄弟飛行 , 沒有人會去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們發現了幾天後 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證據證明 , 萊恩是錯的:那天天敵兄弟飛行了 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個很驚人的發現 , 我會改善你的技術 , 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	首先 , 他沒有有錢 , 他沒有有名所以他辭去了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了你做的事 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信的 , 你就會吸引那些相信你相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你相信的人呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做 「 法律 」 的法律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道這個詞 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	第一個2.5%的人口就是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%人口是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你的早期主要 , 你的大部份和你的早期 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	人們買到手機的唯一理由是 , 因為你不能買到手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在各式各樣的領域中 , 儘管如此 , 創新告訴我們 , 如果你想要大規模市場的執行 , 或大規模市場的執行 , 你就無法做到這一點 , 直到你達成了18%的市場投入 , 最後 , 整個系統就會出現 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新商業的反應是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你們: 「 喔 , 大概10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以試驗超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都只有10%的人會說 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們描述它們的方式 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是腸道的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就這樣做 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你在做商業之前 , 和那些沒有人做事業的人 , 會有什麼樣的感覺 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 在這裡 , 這個小小的差距 , 如傑佛瑞•摩爾所謂的 「 破壞 」 , 因為 , 你看到 , 最早的大部份不會嘗試 , 直到有人嘗試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期的採取者 , 他們很舒適地做出這些決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒適地做出那些直覺決策他們相信世界 , 而不只是產品的產品
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站在六個小時購買iphone , 當他們第一次出櫃時 , 只要走進商店 , 就可以買一台iphone , 然後買了一台iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面螢幕電視上 , 即便當他們第一次出席時 , 甚至是科技的品質 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為科技很棒 , 他們自己也做得到 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你所做的事 , 去買你做的事 , 以及你所做的事 , 為你所做的事 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做些事情證明他們相信什麼 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	有人買了iphone在六小時之內 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們想要如何看待他們:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了你做的事 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 有著名的成功 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 有名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說的 , 成功是金錢和權利市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你應該成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從19年前到19年前 , 到目前為止 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 沒錯 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受歡迎 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我是說 , 我們用 「 反彈 」 的詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我把東西放在我的垃圾桶裡 , 時間華納dvr 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一個商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 股票大約30到40美金 , 然後就被賣掉 , 結果是30到40美元 , 而且從來沒有被販賣過 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它甚至是超過六個 , 除了幾個小的案例上 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看到 , 當tivo發出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們所擁有的一切
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 暫停生活電視 , 錄製電視 , 記住電視 , 記住電視 , 記住電視 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 沒有你問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	古典的主人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不需要它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是這樣的人 , 無論你生活中的每個人 , 都能對你的人生有所貢獻 , 男孩 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它暫停生活電視 , 滑行 , 記住電視 , 記住電視 , 記住電視 , 記住電視 , 記住電視 , 等等 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 , 為你所做的事 , 為你所做的事 , 為你所做的事而做的事 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的例子 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25000人在華盛頓特區去聽見金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們寄出沒有邀請 , 沒有網站去檢查約會 。
how do you do that ?	你該怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士並不是美國唯一一個偉大的人 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是唯一在美國受苦的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有告訴人們需要改變美國 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他走過來告訴別人他相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	我相信: 「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的人 , 相信他所相信的原因 , 他們做出了自己 , 而且他們也被告知了 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些那些人創造了結構 , 讓這個字變得更加人人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	沒錯 , 有250 , 000人在右邊的時間聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人給他看 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們展現自己 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國 , 讓他們在八小時站在8個小時站在8個小時站在8個小時站在華盛頓的美國 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 而不是黑人的白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界中有兩種法律:那些是由一個較高權威的權威所組成的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有法律都由我們所擁有的法律所組成的法律 , 由我們所居住的法律所組成的法律 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	民權運動是完美的 , 幫助他帶來他帶來生命的原因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追求他 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一下 , 他給了我一個 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個夢想 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在 , 聽政治人物 , 他們的12point計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們並不激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權力的權力 , 但那些領導人會鼓舞我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們追蹤那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追蹤那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	這些人是從 「 為何 」 的能力來啟發他們 , 來鼓舞他們的人 , 或找到其他人鼓舞他們 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你在哪裡 ? 怎麼知道你在哪裡 ? 神經學家尼爾•巴格斯研究神經元素 , 把你的車子放在正確的方向 , 神經學家尼爾•巴格斯研究我們周圍的神經元素 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、探索、神經科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾•布吉斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們公開車子時 , 我們要如何記得我們停車在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這裡有個問題面向家人 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們從海馬體開始 , 在黃色 , 這是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在阿茲海默症的傷害 , 除了你停車的位置 , 你就無法記住 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	在拉丁文 「 海馬 」 的名字後 , 它的名字是 「 海馬 」 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和其他大腦一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會互相溝通 , 透過傳遞或連接的電力傳遞訊息 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩個細胞組成的 , 它們非常密切相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解 , 透過記錄的神經元在老鼠、老鼠、老鼠或老鼠身上做些什麼 , 只要他們想知道哪些特性記憶是如何運作的 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們會想像我們正在記錄從一個神經元的海馬體 , 到這裡的海馬體 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出電力時 , 會有一個紅點點 , 點點點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到的是這個神經元知道 , 當老鼠進入一個特定的地方時 , 牠的環境中就會發生 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它訊號到大腦的訊號 , 傳送一個小電動脈 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以顯示出神經元的功能是動物的特定位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從很多不同的神經元發出 , 我們會看到不同神經元的不同神經元 , 會發現不同的神經元會從不同的神經元發出 , 像在這個廣場的盒子裡 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們把腦部的圖片放到腦中 , 說: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	癲癇患者有時候需要電力活動在他們的大腦監控 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人在小鎮上玩電玩遊戲 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	當它們穿過特殊的位置時 , 就會開始發送電脈衝 , 讓它們穿過特殊的位置 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 細胞知道哪個位置 , 位置在哪裡 , 或人在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線是很重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	頂端的頂端 , 像是在箱子的牆壁之間打開空氣 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴展到這個盒子時 , 飛行器就會擴展 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	一旦接觸到南方 , 就會有牆接近南方 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一個牆放到另一邊牆上 , 在盒子裡的細胞 , 就會在盒子裡接觸到南方的細胞 , 另一壁牆就在盒子裡 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這種預測會讓你在周圍的距離和方向 , 了解到海馬體的距離和方向 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	實際上 , 在海馬體中 , 細胞發現了海馬體的特定位置 , 牠在海馬體的位置 , 到海馬迴 , 發現牠在海馬體的位置 , 牠在探索海馬迴時 , 會發現牠在海馬體的位置 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的圖形是 , 你可以看到 , 它的火焰會被周圍的圍繞圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈圈的牆壁就像是邊緣
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的這張圖片 , 左邊邊緣的空氣 , 不管是左邊邊緣的牆 , 或牆壁或甚至兩張桌子之間的距離 , 都可以被拆除 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	因此 , 我們認為細胞決定在哪裡 , 牠在探索的地方 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物品的樣子 , 比如這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你在車子裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們所記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 他們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。

in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個案例中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的形狀和尺寸是如何改變的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果旗子在一個小平方形的環境下 , 你就會看到 , 舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境大大 , 你會看到 , 舉個例子 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境大大 , 他們認為旗幟在一個小方形的環境下 , 該怎麼做 , 但你讓環境更大 , 他們認為旗幟已經被延伸出去 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	正如你所想像的 , 在那個位置的位置 , 那個位置的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這指導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們正在經歷運動 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 假如我們能融合這條路徑 , 我們就知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們能整合這條路徑 , 應該要回頭的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	細胞也得到了一種細胞 , 叫做網絡細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網狀細胞被發現 , 再次在海馬體上 , 牠們有點像細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但現在 , 當老鼠探索時 , 每一個細胞都會在一個很奇妙的平行軌道上 , 都在一個非常平凡的軌道上 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾個網格細胞的網格圖案中 , 每一個細胞的網格圖案 , 都跟其他細胞的網格相互交換 , 和其他細胞的網格相互作用 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以 , 紅色的綠色在這個上面的紅色 , 上面的藍色 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 同樣的 , 老鼠可以在地圖上找到一個虛擬的網絡 , 用三角形來調整它的環境 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	隨著它移動 , 電動活動可以從一個細胞到下一個細胞 , 到下一個細胞去追蹤它的位置 , 所以它可以用它的動作來控制它 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有電網嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於大腦中所有特定部位的神經活動 , 可以改變根據我們是否在六個方向或跑道上運作 , 這意味著神經活動的神經活動 , 每一個網格的網絡都有相同的指標 , 也就是說 , 這意味著神經活動 , 大腦中的每一個特定部位 , 都可以改變根據我們是否在六個方向跑步 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放到mri掃描器裡 , 用一個磁共振造影像我展示給你們看的 , 看看這個訊號 。

so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他在車子的位置 , 和方向去延伸建築物和邊界的位置 , 讓他停下來 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這會代表的是神經細胞的神經細胞 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從車輛停車場所留下的路徑 , 它會代表在網格細胞的路上 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以讓細胞發燒 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到地位的位置 , 在那裡他停車開車的位置 , 找到最好的位置 , 位置在他的大腦中 , 位置在他的大腦中 , 位置在他的大腦中 , 位置的位置是哪裡 , 哪裡是最好的 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個位置不視覺的視覺暗示 , 像是他的車子是否存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許它已經被灌輸了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道那是哪裡 , 所以他知道他要去哪裡 , 拿到它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶力之外 , 如果我們看看這個網狀的圖像在整個腦部紀錄 , 我們看到它在整個腦部的運作 , 我們在整個腦中看到它 , 我們看到它在整整一系列的記錄 , 我們在整個腦中看到它 , 我們看到它在整個大腦裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它在整個腦部裡 , 我們看到它 ,
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是神經機制 , 代表在我們周圍的環境中 , 會產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們就能重新創造出視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重新創造出視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重新創造出視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重新創造出視覺影像 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 透過這些密集的神經細胞 , 來創造出你周遭的空間結構 , 來創造你周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 我沒有提到 , 腦部的細胞 , 正面臨的方向 , 我還沒提到 , 他們火火就像一個對方的指標 。

so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以這只是一個新的時代在認知神經科學領域我們開始了解心理過程 , 例如你如何記住或想像或甚至思考一下 , 由數十億個神經元組成的神經元組成我們的大腦 。

imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全的開放源源是詹姆斯•史塔利斯•史蒂夫、政府、私人部門和公共 , 不只如此遠遠的希望開放源源 , 它是詹姆斯•史密斯的大眾 , 它是詹姆斯•史密斯的大眾 , 它是詹姆斯•史迪斯史上最高的總統 , 他分享了來自近期的軍方歷史 , 來解釋為何保守未來應該要建造橋樑 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球性的議題、開放源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史維利:他是怎麼看待全球安全的 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談談開放安全的安全 , 因為我們在21世紀的安全要更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我開始說 , 咱們來回二十世紀 , 來看看二十世紀 , 這對我們來說是怎樣的安全感 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是巴特 , 法國的北方 , 位於北方 , 位於北方的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年 , 約有70萬人被殺死 , 大約有2 , 000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你在第二次世界大戰結束時 , 會看到戰役 , 三百天 , 三百天 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續嘗試建造牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從戰爭的第一次世界大戰結束 , 第二次世界大戰結束 , 接著我們進入冷戰 , 伊隆的曲線 , 一間聖戰 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	今天我所說的 , 是不是要建造橋樑 , 而是要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	河流的橋樑 , 由伊斯蘭教授和巴爾卡河的主題 , 和巴爾幹的一小部分 , 和巴爾幹大樓的一小部分 , 並且談到 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹的大樓中 , 發生了什麼事 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 幾十年來 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 開始看到這些社區開始 , 開始看到這些社區開始 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會爭論 , 公開資源安全是關聯國際、私人的公共空間 , 並且將它們聯繫起來 , 公開資源安全是連結國際、私人的公共空間 , 並且將它們聯繫起來 , 建立在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我稍稍說明一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球共同點 , 都在受到威脅的威脅 , 以至全球常見 , 都受到威脅的威脅 , 以至全球常常被打破 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是很明顯的 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一艘船 , 一艘船 , 橫跨印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	牠會在牠的旁邊 , 帶著保險套 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	這樣才能防止海盜來防止海盜 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	piracy是極具威脅性的威脅 , 在印度的海洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	陰謀也非常活躍在馬拉克卡 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	牠在瓜地馬尼亞海灣游泳 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	這是在全球運輸系統中數十億美金的損失 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20個船員 , 500名馬丁爾斯特 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是全球常見的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉換不同的海洋 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	那時 , 他們被監禁 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一項信用卡詐欺 , 給他們超過十億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 網路犯罪的2兆美元在全球經濟上 。
two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在英國的大英國 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網路海 , 我們知道無限的基本上是極端的基礎 , 絕對是極端的基礎 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	另一件我擔心的事情是 , 全球普通的威脅是威脅 , 被販賣的威脅 , 從阿富汗 , 到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心古柯鹼來自東南北部 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心人口販賣 , 和販賣 , 最重要的是 , 也許 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 和販賣 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	販賣大量在海洋中 , 同時也在全球共通點上 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴各位 , 這是個非常高科技的美國海軍軍隊 , 用來阻止販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這種病患藥品牌會被毒品包裹起來 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它在南美的叢林中被建造出來 。

crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	第四個 , 複雜的溝通 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種人口販賣 , 包括毒品、武器、大規模毀滅的武器 , 都是威脅到全球普通的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	咱們在阿富汗舉辦這場演講 。

eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	全世界的百分之八十 , 鴉片和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也知道 , 恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是蓋達組織所在的地方 。

so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以恐怖主義擔憂了全球常見的一部分 , 我們必須解決 。
so here we are , 21st century .	這裡是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們二十世紀的工具並不會成功 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會把安全帶到槍枝的邊緣 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會把安全帶在槍枝上 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要應用軍事力量 。

but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 公開資源安全是國際間 , 公開資源安全 , 國際間 , 私人交流 , 開放資源安全是國際、互聯網 , 和私人交流的連結 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子 , 說明這如何運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗軍人 。
they are all holding books .	他們全都包含書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 , 我以為我讀了這個人口統計數字 , 年輕男子和女性 , 在2030歲時 , 很像在阿富汗 。 」
you would be correct .	你是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%無法讀到阿富汗的安全力量 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班教育在期待這些男人和婦女可以學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以 , 問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們正在教導他們在讀書中 , 用私人部門和開發機構的關係 , 來處理私人部門和發展機構 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們教了超過200 , 000阿富汗安全部隊 , 來閱讀和寫字 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你讀和寫在阿富汗 , 你通常會把筆放在你的口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男人和女人畢業時 , 他們拿著一筆很棒的驕傲 , 然後把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這裡有50個國家參與這個任務 , 國際間有50個國家參與這個任務:這些發展機構和私人和公共機構 , 都參與這個任務 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也教他們對抗技巧 , 但我會說 , 開放式安全的連結 , 來創造更長時間的安全性 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。

they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	此外 , 在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸 , 營養了病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	一般來說 , 他們會有四十萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是被軍事的組成 , 而是由軍事組成 , 包括人道組織:手術希望 , 微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織把志工投入 。
interagency physicians come out .	醫師來到這裡 。
they're all part of this .	它們都是這一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 和他的母親兩天來到眼科診所 , 來到眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被完整時 , 他突然抬起頭 , 說: 「 媽媽 , 維羅•伊斯維羅 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	乘以四十萬個病人治療 , 這種私人和安全力量的力量 , 你開始看到創造安全力量的力量 , 非常不同的方式 。

you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須把這二十個世紀的財務分開 , 如同我所說的 , 我們的軍事是創造出21世紀安全的安全、國際、、私人的 , 和交互溝通的力量 , 才能成為創造21世紀安全的安全、國際、私人和公共事務的力量 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我會說我們今天早上聽到的 , 維基百科 。 我用維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 全都不用維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 全都不用維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 都不用維基百科 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每一天 , 每一天 , 有數萬人 , 每天都在寫信息 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這是個完美的圖片 , 沒有人和我們所有人都一樣聰明 。
